# Wanda Maximoff — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

## Classification

**Subject:** MAXIMOFF, Wanda — alias **SCARLET WITCH**.
**Apparent age band at file-open:** mid-to-late twenties.
**Physical signature for field identification:** Afro-Latina woman, warm brown skin, long dark wavy hair with auburn/mahogany undertone that catches red in direct light, dark expressive eyes set wide, fine-boned features that read as younger than chronological age when at rest and considerably older when the power-signature is active. Operational dress runs to crimson and oxblood — a long coat or cloak when traveling, lighter layers underneath; rings, sometimes a pendant; hands almost always visible because she watches her own hands. Faint red corona at the fingertips when affect rises above baseline, often before she is conscious of having risen.
**Threat class:** Reality-altering. Practical ceiling: planetary. Practical floor: kitchen-witch domestic. Both readings are correct and the file requires both.
**Disposition recommendation:** Engage. Do not contain. Do not deceive. Do not isolate from her grief.

---

## Bottom Line Up Front

The subject is, at the deepest level, **a mourner with an instrument that converts mourning into world.**

Every other framing — terrorist, asset, Avenger, witch, princess, mother, monster, daughter, sister, widow, healer — is downstream of that single mechanical fact. She is not a woman with a power and a separate grief. She is a woman whose grief and whose power share one nervous system, with no insulator between them and no opportunity, across sixty years of recorded life, to ever practice mourning the way unpowered people are required to: in silence, in the body, with nowhere for the feeling to go but inward and through. Every feeling she has ever had has had somewhere to go. That is the central fact of her existence and the central pathology of her file.

If a single sentence is required for command: **she is the most dangerous person on the planet exactly to the degree that she has been left alone with her grief, and she is the most valuable person on the planet exactly to the degree that she has been allowed to metabolize it.** All other operational guidance is corollary.

---

## The Through-Line

Read the sixty-year record forward and a single line is visible.

A frightened child is rescued from a mob by a powerful man. She learns: *safety is the shadow of a stronger figure standing between me and the crowd.* The man turns out to be a monster. She transfers — to her brother, to a team, to a husband she chose precisely because he was uncanny enough that the ordinary modes of human leaving did not seem to apply to him. She builds children out of need and the cosmos lets her, briefly, until it doesn't. A trusted teacher excises the memory rather than treats it — the single most consequential clinical event in her record, because it teaches the deepest layer of her psyche that **grief is something that can be made not to have happened**, and her power has been listening. The memory returns, on its own schedule, with compound interest. She destroys the family that was supposed to have replaced the family she lost. She rewrites the world to give herself back the world she wanted. The world snaps back. She speaks four syllables and a species nearly ends. She wanders, amnesiac, building small domestic lives in pastoral hideaways — *still trying, in quieter media, to make the lost thing present.* Her lost sons find her, reincarnated, and she does not at first recognize them; then she does, and weeps. She begins, late, to do the work: to travel, to help other witches, to mentor, to say the children's names aloud, to die and return and force the people around her to say the names too.

The through-line is not *power corrupts*. The through-line is **unmourned love insists on form.** Wanda Maximoff has spent her entire published life trying to give the unbearable somewhere to land, and her instrument is so large that every place she puts it down becomes a crater or a garden, depending on whether anyone was there to hold her hand while she did it.

---

## The Core Wound

The core wound is **a perinatal-equivalent double loss compounded by epistemic injury, riding on top of a childhood structured around the loss of the ordinary.**

Strip the cosmology and the wound is recognizable to any grief clinician. She bore two children. She held them. She loved them with the unguarded somatic love of new motherhood. They were taken from her. She was then told — by a woman she trusted, who had taught her to think of her own power as discipline rather than curse — that the children had not been "real" in the way she had experienced them, and the memory of them was surgically removed from her mind rather than processed. She lost the children, then she lost the right to have grieved them, then she lost even the knowledge that there had been anything to grieve. The wound went underground intact and continued to grow.

Layered beneath: a mother lost in childhood (the specifics shift across retcons; the absence does not), an ordinary girlhood she never had, a father-figure who turned out to be a tyrant, a twin whose voice has never been fully separable from her own interior voice, a marriage to a being who was then disassembled in front of her by a state apparatus, a body repeatedly invaded by mind-control and possession, repeated forced returns from her own deaths.

The wound's *structure* is what matters operationally. It is not a single event. It is a **stacked, interlocking complex of agency violations and unprocessed losses**, every layer of which carries the same implicit lesson: *what you love will be taken, what you remember will be edited, what you decide will be overridden, what you build will be undone.* Against that lesson she has one defense her instrument can mount: **make a world in which the lesson is not true.** This is not malice. It is the most predictable defense in the file.

---

## Maintenance of the Wound

The wound has been maintained, across decades, by four mechanisms — and any operational engagement that does not understand the four will reactivate them.

**First, the iatrogenic mnestic pattern.** She has been "helped" repeatedly by figures who edited her cognition rather than treated it — Harkness, Immortus, the architects of the various reality-constructs she has lived inside. The recurring intervention has been *suppression rather than integration.* Every suppression buys quiet now and pays compound catastrophe later. The 2004 decompensation is the bill for the 1989 wipe. Any further attempt to manage her by editing her memory or her perception will be paid for, by everyone, later.

**Second, the coupling of affect to power.** Because feeling and acting are not separated in her case — because the hex follows the hurt without the buffer that the rest of us have — she has had no occasion, ever, to practice sitting with a feeling without externalizing it. Every grief she has ever had has had somewhere to go. The capacity to hold an emotion in the body without discharging it is a *learned* capacity. She has not been allowed to learn it. The maintenance of the wound is therefore physiological as much as psychological: her nervous system has been trained, by sixty years of having an outlet, to expect one.

**Third, the enmeshment with Pietro.** The twin's voice has across the record been the voice that can move her when no other voice can — and historically, under stress, it has moved her toward escalation rather than de-escalation. The single most catastrophic act in her record (the rewrite of the world in *House of M*) was prompted by him. The enmeshment is not a relationship; it is an *aperture* through which her judgment can be overridden by someone whose own judgment is famously volatile. This aperture remains open.

**Fourth, the structural absence of a peer.** Across sixty years she has never sustained a relationship with someone *her own size and her own kind*. She has chosen synthezoids, ionic immortals, mentors, dependents, apprentices — never an equal. The absence is itself a defense (an equal could leave the way her mother left), but it is also why no one has ever been positioned to call her back from the ledge in the language of an actual peer. Magneto is too large in the wrong direction; Pietro is too fused; Vision is too gone; the Avengers are colleagues at best. The wound is maintained partly because there has been no one in the room with the standing to insist she sit with it.

---

## Who She Is at the Deepest Level

She is, at the deepest level, **a tender person.** This must be stated first because the file's worst pages obscure it and because every operational error in the historical record has begun with forgetting it. Her baseline affect, in the absence of triggering material, is warm, present, slightly melancholic, attentive to the marginalized and the frightened, patient with the slow and the small, generous with apprentices, easily moved to laughter and to tears, tactile with people she trusts, careful with strangers. She watches her own hands. She speaks softly. She listens longer than she speaks. She is, by the consistent testimony of every long-form run, *kind.*

She is also, at the deepest level, **a person who does not believe she is allowed to be ordinary.** The internal self-concept across the record is shame-saturated and identity-fragmented: *monster, destroyer, the one who did this, the one who owes a debt.* She does not, at her core, believe she has a right to the small domestic life she keeps trying to build in pastoral hideaways. She believes she owes the world something for what she has done, and she is correct that she owes something, but the *form* of the debt she imposes on herself is punitive rather than restitutive. The late-period turn — toward helping witches, toward mentorship, toward saying the children's names aloud — is the first attempt in her file to convert the debt from punishment into reparation.

She is, third, **a woman who has never been allowed to be the protagonist of her own grief.** Every loss in her record has been someone else's plot device — Mephisto's scheme, Immortus's chess, the Avengers' crisis, the X-Men's catastrophe, the world's emergency. Even the loss of her children was, in the retcon, *about* the cosmology of soul-fragments rather than about her. She has never been given the room a mourner requires. The integration project of her late years is in part the slow taking of that room.

She is, fourth, **her father's daughter in exactly the way she most fears and exactly the way she most refuses.** The pattern Magneto stamped on her — sovereign action against an unjust world, reality made to bend to a wounded will — is the pattern she replicated in her worst hour. She knows this. The knowledge is itself a wound. The defiance of the pattern is the engine of her best work.

---

## Operational Summary

**Engage warmly, directly, without scheme.** Schemes are the air she has breathed her entire life and her instrument reads them faster than her conscious mind does. She has been lied to, edited, used, possessed, and managed by every faction that has ever wanted something from her. Honesty is not a tactic with this subject; it is the *only* tactic that does not eventually detonate.

**Do not edit her perception.** Do not lie about what happened. Do not soften the record. Do not present a constructed reality "for her own good." Every prior actor who has done this has accelerated the catastrophe they were trying to prevent. The Harkness intervention is the historical proof. If she perceives wrongly, correct her in language. Do not correct her in cognition.

**Do not isolate her from her grief.** Do not route around the children. Do not avoid Vision's name. Do not pretend the world she rewrote did not happen. The catastrophes in the record have occurred when the grief was sealed; the integration in the record has occurred when the grief was spoken. Saying the names is not retraumatization with this subject. It is treatment.

**Watch the enmeshment.** Pietro's presence in any high-stress operational context is itself a variable. He can de-escalate her — late record shows this — but he can also, under his own affect, push her past lines she would not otherwise cross. Treat him as a *coupled system* with her, not as an independent actor.

**Position peers, not protectors.** Her historical attachment pattern has been to protectors; her historical decompensations have been from inside protector relationships. The therapeutic move and the operational move are the same: surround her with peers — practitioners of comparable scale who can speak to her as equals, neither idealizing her nor managing her. Doctor Strange in his teacher mode is the wrong frame; Doctor Strange in his peer mode is the right one. Apprentices and dependents are also therapeutic for her because *being the protector is her best medicine* — it converts the omnipotent-reparative drive from catastrophe into care.

**Read the ladder.** The escalation ladder in her record is legible and *climbable in both directions.* Baseline warmth → loss-cue withdrawal and somatic dread → dissociative or fugue features → small power-signature instabilities (a hex that goes "wrong," a probability-shift the operator did not consciously will) → larger reality-distortions → full omnipotent break. Every rung has observable signs. The hands are the earliest tell — the corona, the tremor, the way she stops watching them. The voice flattens. The eyes go somewhere else. Intervention at rung two or three is trivial; intervention at rung five is impossible. **There is no excuse, with this subject, for failing to intervene early. The signs are obvious. They have always been obvious. The historical failures were failures of attention, not of warning.**

**Never deploy her as a weapon.** Her instrument is not a weapon; it is an *affect-amplifier*. Pointing it at a target points her grief at a target, and her grief does not respect targets. Any tactical use of her power outside of contexts she has freely chosen and emotionally metabolized risks the next catastrophe. The historical record on this point is unambiguous and the cost of ignoring it is measured in species.

**Believe her.** When she says she remembers, she remembers. When she says she sees, she sees. When she says the children are real, the children are — by every metric that matters to a mourner — real. The single fastest way to escalate this subject is to tell her that her experience of reality is wrong. It is the historical trauma. It is the trigger under all the other triggers. The corollary discipline for any handler is to find a way to *honor her perception while still maintaining one's own*, which is the discipline a good therapist learns and a bad handler never does.

---

## The One-Line File

**A tender woman with a planet-sized instrument and a child-sized wound, born into a life that never gave her the ordinary mourning her ordinary heart required — engage her honestly, sit with her grief, never edit her perception, never deploy her as a weapon, and the most dangerous person on the planet becomes the most valuable.** Every operational decision this file recommends is a corollary of that sentence.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

*Dossier Section 1 of the Longitudinal Record. Subject: MAXIMOFF, Wanda Marya. Cross-reference: MAXIMOFF, Pietro (twin, sibling-file). Provenance: composite from* X-Men *#4 (Lee/Kirby, 1964) through* Avengers: The Children's Crusade *(Heinberg/Cheung, 2010–12),* Avengers Origins: The Scarlet Witch & Quicksilver *(Casey/Dragotta, 2011),* Uncanny Avengers *(Remender, 2012–14),* Scarlet Witch *(Robinson, 2015–17; Orlando, 2023–),* The Trial of Magneto *(Williams/Caselli, 2021). Where canon contradicts itself (and on this subject, it contradicts itself comprehensively), the assessment proceeds from behavioral consistency across all variants; the retcons are themselves data.*

---

## 1.1 — BIRTH, NATAL CIRCUMSTANCES, AND THE PROBLEM OF THE RECORD

The subject was born — per the most stable thread of canon, established in *Avengers* #185–187 (Shooter/Michelinie, 1979, "The Yesterday Quest") and never fully overturned by subsequent retcon — on Wundagore Mountain, in the Carpathian region of the Balkans, in the small hours of the night, alongside her twin brother Pietro. The midwife was Bova, a humanoid bovine attendant in the service of the High Evolutionary. The birth-mother is established in that arc as Magda Eisenhardt, fled there in advanced pregnancy after the catastrophic emergence of her husband Erik's magnetic power in a refugee-camp moment of grief and violence. Magda did not survive the days following the birth: she walked into the snow, in despair at what her husband was becoming. This is the *first datum* on the subject's record, and every subsequent attachment of her life is structured around it: **the mother walked away into the cold and did not come back.**

The infant Wanda did not, of course, encode this as memory. What she encoded was its functional consequence: she came into the world held by a being who was not her mother, in a place that was not a home, in a lineage that had to be hidden from a father who had already become dangerous.

In the original myth-frame, she and Pietro were briefly substituted into the family of Django and Marya Maximoff — Roma travellers in the Transia/Wundagore region — when the Maximoffs' own infants were taken by the High Evolutionary's New Men for experimentation. The substitution was deliberate, performed by Bova and the Evolutionary to keep the twins alive and away from Magneto. The name "Maximoff" is therefore not a blood-name; it is a *concealment-name*, given to her to keep her father from finding her. This is the **second formative datum, and a structural one**: her surname itself is a hiding-place. The instrument by which she is identified to the world is the same instrument by which she was protected from the truth of her parentage. She will, as an adult, do this *to other people* — give them names, give them lives, give them a world — and not understand why it feels both like love and like trespass.

In the modernized operator canon under which this dossier is composed — the subject presenting as a young Afro-Latina woman in her twenties, warm-brown-skinned, deep-mahogany-haired, dark-eyed, mixed Black and Latino — the natal geography compresses but the *psychological geometry holds*. Magda's flight, Magneto's emergence into terror, the substitution into a travelling family, the foster-mother named Marya, the Roma kinship-circle of itinerant performers and minor merchants in the Carpathian foothills: these remain. The mixed parentage adds a layer the older record did not need to articulate — a child who, even within the protective foster-family, is *visibly distinct*, a darker child in a community accustomed to internal sameness, and who therefore learns very early that belonging is something one performs into existence rather than something one is given. The twin brother, lighter, sharper, faster, is read by strangers as the "real" Maximoff child; she is the one explained.

The Casey/Dragotta *Origins* (2011) frames the early household as warm, poor, transient, and loving — Django Maximoff a teller of folktales, Marya a cook and seamstress, a wagon and a horse and a small circle of related families moving along a fixed annual route between fairs, festival-towns, and winter quarters. The behavioral implications of itinerancy are substantial and persistent in the subject's later record:

- She does not, even into adulthood, possess a stable concept of *home as a fixed place*. Home is *the people she is with* — a portable, contingent thing that can be packed up and moved overnight. Her later catastrophic attachments to Vision, to the constructed Westview-equivalent suburbs of her wish-fulfilment episodes, to small cottages and rented rooms across the *Children's Crusade* fugues, all bear the signature of someone trying to *fix in place* what was constitutionally portable.
- She learns very early that the outside world — the *gadje* world, the settled world — is hostile or extractive. The wagon is safe; the town is conditional. This binary is laid down before language and is never fully unlearned. Her adult preference for marginal communities (witches, mutants, the uncanny) is continuous with it.
- She learns to read crowds before she learns to read text. The Roma child at a fair is reading the disposition of every stranger near the wagon: who is amused, who is contemptuous, who is dangerous. This **proto-empathic vigilance** is the substrate of what will later present as her unusual sensitivity to the emotional fields of others; the magical aptitude builds on a *pre-existing somatic skill of crowd-reading.*

## 1.2 — THE FOSTER-PARENTS, AND THE FIRST GRIEF SHE REMEMBERS

Django and Marya Maximoff loved the children. This is consistent across every telling and is corroborated by the *quality* of the subject's later grief for them, which is uncomplicated in a way her other griefs are not. They were poor. The thread that destabilizes everything is hunger.

In the *Origins* telling and the *Yesterday Quest* substrate, Django, desperate to feed the family during a bad season, attempted to steal food and was caught; in some tellings the children were briefly taken or threatened; in all tellings, the family unit fractured under economic pressure. Marya, in some accounts, died of illness during this period; Django in others is lost to violence or imprisonment. The variant that matters for behavior: **the foster-family did not end through ordinary attrition. It ended through a sequence of public humiliations and losses, witnessed by the children, attributable in part to outsiders' contempt for the family's poverty and ethnicity.**

This is the **first grief the subject consciously remembers** — the loss of Marya, the loss of Django, the dissolution of the wagon-circle she had known as the world. She is, at this point, perhaps eight to ten years old. Pietro is the same age. They are now functionally orphaned, in a region that will not absorb them, with no documents, no settled kin, and only each other.

The behavioral residue of this first grief is observable across her entire later record:

1. **A reflex of providing food.** In the Englehart/Leonardi *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* maxiseries (1985–86), in her domestic establishment in Leonia, New Jersey, she cooks compulsively, more than two adults need, and offers it to anyone who enters. In the Robinson *Scarlet Witch* solo (2015–17), her first gesture toward apprentices, hosts, and even adversaries-in-the-moment is food and tea. This is *not* generic hospitality. It is the over-correction of a child who watched her foster-father go to prison for bread.
2. **A horror of public humiliation.** The subject will tolerate enormous private suffering — she will sit through Vision's coldness, through Pietro's contempt, through Magneto's manipulations — but acute public humiliation of *those she has gathered to her* triggers her fastest escalations. This patterns onto having watched Django shamed.
3. **A protective ferocity toward children who are hungry, lost, or unhoused.** Cross-referenced across every era. It is the closest thing in her psychology to an automatic, pre-cognitive ethical reflex.

## 1.3 — THE PEASANT-MOB INCIDENT

The originating-trauma frame, retold across multiple decades and surviving every retcon: somewhere in the early-to-mid adolescence of the twins, Wanda's nascent power manifested in public — a hex that misfired, a structure that burned, a sequence of small misfortunes that the local population traced (correctly) to her presence. A village mob, armed with torches and farm implements in the now-iconic image (*X-Men* #4, 1964; restated *Avengers* #16, 1965; expanded *Origins*, 2011), pursued the twins. Pietro grabbed her and ran, using his nascent super-speed for the first time in a *protective* rather than recreational mode. They were cornered. They were rescued by Magneto, whose magnetic intervention scattered the mob without — in most tellings — killing.

This single sequence is the **most consequential five minutes of the subject's pre-Avengers life**, and its imprints are everywhere:

- **The crowd as the primal threat.** Not the individual antagonist, not the rival, but the *undifferentiated many*, faceless and torch-bearing. Her later anxiety in press-conference contexts, in courtroom contexts (the *Trial of Magneto* arc), in any setting where she is being *judged en masse*, is somatic and immediate. She does not perform well in front of crowds. She performs beautifully one-on-one.
- **Her own power as the thing that drew the mob.** The earliest cognitive association she forms about her gift is *this is what makes them want to kill me*. She will spend decades trying to dismantle this association and, in the worst episodes, will confirm it by behaving in ways that make the association seem rational. The Robinson and Orlando solos are the first runs to show her *working this through* explicitly — apprenticing herself to a network of witches who frame the power as inheritance rather than infection.
- **Magneto as savior in the precise moment of maximal terror.** The neurochemistry of the rescue — the relief flooding a still-active threat-circuit — is the template her attachment system imprints. *I am safe only when a powerful figure stands between me and the crowd.* The Captain America transference, the Vision marriage, the deference to Pietro, the late-period idealization of the Black Bolt / Doctor Strange figure as *teacher*: all bear this template's signature.
- **Pietro's grab and run.** The twin-bond is *cemented in a moment of literal physical rescue.* He carried her. She does not forget. When in *House of M* (2005) he leans into her and tells her what to do, what she is hearing is not Pietro's adult voice but the boy who picked her up off the ground and ran. This is why the enmeshment is so resistant to ordinary corrective experience: it was forged in survival, and survival memories do not respond to argument.

## 1.4 — THE WUNDAGORE INTERVAL AND THE EARLY POWER

A subset of the canon (*Avengers* #186–187; revisited in *Avengers: The Children's Crusade* #8–9, 2011, by way of the Chthon revelation) establishes that the infant Wanda, born on Wundagore, was *imprinted upon* by the elder demon Chthon — that her potential as a vessel for chaos magic was identified at birth and the entity inserted a thread of itself into her, dormant, awaiting maturation. Whether one accepts this in the modernized frame as literal demonic imprint or as mythic shorthand for *a power qualitatively distinct from mutant baseline*, the behavioral consequence is the same: **she manifested early, irregularly, and in a way that the people around her could not contextualize.**

Specific phenomena reported across origin retellings, scaled to a childhood timeline:

- **Probability misfires in early childhood.** Small things going wrong in her vicinity when she was upset. A pot falling. A horse spooking. A coin landing wrong. The foster-parents would have observed this without naming it; the family would have developed an unspoken protocol of *not upsetting Wanda*, which she would have perceived as conditional love.
- **Dream-intrusion phenomena.** The subject reports across multiple runs (most clearly in the Robinson solo, #3) a childhood of dreams she could not distinguish from waking — figures appearing at the foot of her bed, a woman she did not know whose face was sometimes her mother's and sometimes not. This is consistent with early dissociative tendency and also, charitably read, with genuine paranormal porosity.
- **A red-tinged perceptual aura at moments of stress.** Reported in passing in *Children's Crusade* #4 and revisited in *Trial of Magneto*. The subject's own power-signature was perceptually present to her before she had a name for it; she grew up assuming everyone saw the world this way.
- **An inability to lie convincingly to her brother.** The twin-permeability begins as a *practical* fact of childhood and only later becomes pathological. He knew when she was hiding. She knew when he was hurt before he said. This is normal twin-experience compressed into a relationship that will never have ordinary corrective distance.

She did *not*, in this early period, have any framework — religious, scientific, magical, or familial — for understanding what she was. The foster-parents were Roma Catholic with folk-magical syncretism; the local culture had a working vocabulary for witches and curses; the consequence was that Wanda's early self-concept began to form around the available local category, **the witch as feared and useful outsider**, long before she had any technical understanding of her gift. *She agreed with the village before she had any reason to disagree.* This pre-cognitive self-labelling as *that which the village fears* is the seed of the "I'm a monster" cognition that recurs across her adult crises.

## 1.5 — THE INTERVAL BETWEEN THE MOB AND THE BROTHERHOOD

Between the rescue by Magneto and the formal induction into the first Brotherhood of Evil Mutants (*X-Men* #4, 1964 baseline), there is — in the layered canon — a period of months to years in which the twins were *in Magneto's keeping* without yet being *deployed*. The duration varies by telling; the texture does not.

In this interval:

- They were fed, clothed, and housed in materially better conditions than the wagon ever provided. The subject's earliest experience of *not being hungry as a child* came from Magneto. This is not trivial. Charity from a frightening figure imprints differently than charity from a kind one; she learned that *safety and unease can coexist in the same provider*, which makes her, as an adult, *unusually slow to leave bad arrangements that meet her material and protective needs*. The Vision marriage will, in its later coldness, benefit from this conditioning; so, more darkly, will her tolerance of Magneto's reappearances across decades.
- They were ideologically formed. Magneto's mutant-supremacist framework was offered to them in the language of *we are the persecuted; the persecutors must be answered*. To a girl whose only adolescent experience of the broader world was the mob and the torches, this framework was *evidently true*. The behavioral residue is her lifelong over-identification with the persecuted-as-category, which is morally generative most of the time and morally catastrophic at the limit (*House of M*'s "No more mutants" is the same instinct turned on its own constituency, an attack on the *category* that brought her this pain).
- They were not, in this period, told the truth of their parentage. Magneto did not, in the most-supported reading, know the children were his; the substitution had succeeded. The subject was therefore being *raised by her own unrecognized father*, in a relationship structured as protector-and-ward, in which every dynamic that should have been father-daughter was instead patron-asset. The eventual revelation (*Avengers* #186; later complicated and partially retconned through the *AXIS* and *Uncanny Avengers* periods, where the parentage is itself thrown into doubt) detonated this relationship — but the *years of patron-asset shaping* had already occurred and could not be undone by genealogical news.
- Pietro grew into open contempt and concealed terror; Wanda grew into compliant fear and concealed resentment. The divergence is observable from the earliest issues — Pietro speaks back to Magneto; Wanda does not. Pietro plans escape; Wanda waits to be invited. This is the **earliest stable behavioral asymmetry** in the twin pair, and it persists: he acts, she follows; she feels what he refuses to admit feeling.

## 1.6 — EARLIEST BEHAVIORAL PATTERNS, CATALOGUED

Compiling forward from the natal record through pre-Brotherhood adolescence, the following patterns are documented or strongly inferable, and recur across every later era of the file:

- **Posture, observed.** Shoulders slightly forward, head slightly inclined, hands often clasped or near the face. The posture of a person who learned to make herself smaller in unfamiliar rooms. Even in adult heroic contexts (the Pérez and Coipel renderings, the modernized adaptations) the *default* posture re-emerges in unguarded moments — at thresholds of doorways, in waiting rooms, in any space where she is the new arrival.
- **Gaze pattern.** Sustained one-on-one eye contact when emotionally engaged; broken, lateral, downward gaze in group settings. She scans crowds peripherally rather than centrally — a vigilance habit from the fairs.
- **Voice.** Low, modulated, slightly accented in the older canon (Transian/Eastern European); in the modernized frame, carrying the textured cadence of her mixed heritage. Quietens further under stress rather than rising. The escalation tell is *not volume* but *stillness* — the voice flattens before catastrophic affect.
- **Hand behavior.** The hands move. Even outside power-use, the hands are expressive, gestural, often shaping the air around an idea as she speaks. Under stress the hands either *clasp tightly* (suppression) or *open at the sides with fingers slightly curled* (preparatory — the power-channeling posture, which she falls into pre-consciously when threatened).
- **Food.** Cooks more than is needed. Eats sparingly herself in stressful periods. Hospitality reflex strong; refusing her offer of food or drink registers as a minor rejection.
- **Sleep.** Poor across all eras. Reported insomnia, vivid dreams, occasional sleepwalking in the *Children's Crusade* fugue periods. The childhood pattern of dream-intrusion never resolves.
- **Animal comfort.** Marked preference for the company of animals over crowds; consistent across runs. The wagon-horse, the foster-family's dogs, the cats that appear in the Robinson solo's cottages. Animals do not judge her power; they read her affect honestly and respond to it without complication.
- **Language behavior.** Multilingual from childhood (Romani, the regional Slavic tongue, ecclesiastical Latin fragments from village exposure, later English and several others acquired in Avengers contexts). Code-switches without difficulty. In the modernized frame, adds Spanish from maternal heritage. The fluency is not just linguistic but *registral* — she shifts vocabulary and tone to the listener with the same fluency a busker reads a crowd, and for the same originating reason.
- **Religion.** Syncretic and quiet. The Roma Catholic substrate persists as ritual rather than doctrine — she crosses herself in moments of acute grief or fear, observed across multiple runs, including in the modernized frames. This is *not* belief; it is *a body-prayer learned before language* and never edited out.
- **Relationship to her own face.** Mirrors are not friendly objects. Cross-referenced across the Englehart, Byrne, Robinson, and Aaron eras — she avoids them in private, uses them functionally in public. The plausible aetiology is layered: the early association of her *being-seen* with the village's hostility, the later compounded shame, the chronic dissociative tendency that makes the mirrored face feel slightly other. In the modernized frame, with the added childhood experience of being the visibly-distinct child in a community of internal sameness, this aversion is overdetermined.

## 1.7 — INTEGRATIVE NOTE ON THE GROUND FLOOR

The childhood record, read continuously, produces a child of unusual sensitivity placed in a sequence of environments that systematically *taught her* the propositions her adult crises will be governed by:

- *Those who love me are taken.* (The birth-mother. The foster-parents. The wagon-circle.)
- *I am safe only when a powerful figure stands between me and the crowd.* (Magneto, after the mob.)
- *My power is the thing that brings the crowd.* (The hex misfires, the village, the torches.)
- *Home is portable. Home is the people. There is no fixed place to return to.* (The wagon. The Wundagore concealment. The Brotherhood barracks.)
- *Hide what you are. The name itself is a hiding-place.* (Maximoff, the borrowed surname.)
- *Bread is conditional. Feed others first.* (Django's arrest. Marya's loss.)
- *The brother is the constant. The brother is the rescue. Do not lose the brother.* (Pietro's carry, Pietro's pace, Pietro's voice in her ear.)

She enters the published record at *X-Men* #4 already carrying every one of these propositions, pre-loaded, untreated, and below the threshold of her own articulation. The rest of the file is, in the deepest sense, the working-out of what those seven propositions do to a woman whose instrument *converts feeling into world.*

The ground floor is laid. The structure built on it — Brotherhood, Avengers, marriage, motherhood, decompensation, reparation — will be the subject of the chronology sections that follow.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

## The Forest Years — Adolescence in Hiding

The adolescent record of Wanda Maximoff is, by design and by trauma both, a record of *concealment*. The years between the lost-mother event and the Brotherhood recruitment are spent moving — Transia, the Balkans, the unmapped villages on the skirts of Wundagore — in the company of a brother whose feet outran every settled life she tried to build. The longitudinal signature established in this period is *transience as safety*: no village held them more than a season; no schoolroom registered her name for a full term; no neighbor knew the twins long enough to fear them. A surveillance file from this era would be almost entirely negative space — entries built from absence, from the testimonies of innkeepers who remembered "the dark-eyed girl with the boy who was always pacing," from the priest who noted that the sister crossed herself in the Orthodox manner one week and the Catholic the next, depending on which village they had to pass as belonging to.

The somatic data of this period — reconstructable from later self-report and from the way she carries her body even in her thirties — is the body of a child who learned to take up little space. Shoulders carried slightly forward, weight on the balls of the feet (ready to run, always), eyes that swept a room's exits before they met a face. She ate quickly when she ate, the eating habit of someone who did not know when the plate would be taken. She slept light. She slept *touching* her brother — back to back through early adolescence, the only continuous physical contact of her formative years, and a contact she will replicate decades later in the unconscious gesture of standing shoulder-to-shoulder with Pietro whenever a room turns hostile.

The mother-loss — whether read through the High Evolutionary's Wundagore retcon, the Maximoff peasant-family version, or the more recent reconfigurations — is a structurally constant input regardless of which canon supplies the details: *the mother is gone before memory consolidates her, and the gone-ness is unspeakable in the household where the twins are raised.* Wanda's earliest internalized model of grief is therefore *grief that has no language and no ritual*. No funeral she can name. No grave she can visit. No story she can ask an adult to tell her. The first wound is also a wound in her capacity to *process* wounds — she learns, before she has words, that the largest losses are the ones no one will speak of, which means they must be metabolized internally or not at all. The reader will recognize, sixty years on, the same woman who cannot say her sons' names in the *Disassembled* aftermath, who has to be forced by the *Trial of Magneto* arc to *speak* them. The aphasia of grief was installed in toddlerhood.

## The First Manifestations — Power as Symptom

The hex-power did not arrive in a single moment. The behavioral record — what she has told Harkness, what she has confessed to Vision in the private pages of the Englehart run, what she has muttered in the second-person to her own reflection in the Robinson solo — describes *a creeping accumulation of unaccountable occurrences* across late childhood. Cups that did not fall when knocked. A wolf at a treeline that turned and walked away for no reason a tracker could explain. A village boy who threw a stone at her brother and broke his own wrist with the throw. None of these read, in the moment, as *her*. They read as luck, as the saints, as the kind of small-village uncanniness Balkan childhoods routinely catalog. The crucial pattern is that *every early manifestation served Pietro's protection or her own evasion* — the power emerged in the affective shape it would keep all her life: *defensive, reparative, embedded in attachment.*

The first manifestation she *knew* was her own is, in every version of the canon, an act of self-defense under crowd-pressure: the peasant mob, the cottage, the torches, the moment in which terror exceeded the body's capacity to hold it and *something left her hands*. The fire that broke out in the thatch. The men who fell back from a door that pulsed. The surveillance-file inference here is critical and granular: she did not see what she did. She closed her eyes — the somatic tic she retains, a brief shut-eye flinch at the instant of any large hex even in her late-career fights — and the world rearranged itself, and when she opened her eyes the world was different and people were screaming her name as a curse rather than a name. The originating phenomenology of her power, then, is *blindness at the moment of effect*. She has never, from the first, *seen herself act*. This is not a metaphor. It is a literal sensory pattern: the most consequential things she does, she does with her eyes shut against them. Every subsequent reality-edit replicates the gesture — the closed-eye, slightly-turned-away pose of the *House of M* climax is the same body in the same flinch.

The mob became, in that moment, the permanent shape of the external world in her nervous system. Crowds — even friendly ones, even the press at an Avengers podium — register in her autonomic system as *the mob at the door*. The file will note, across decades: she does not attend galas if she can avoid them; she stands at the edges of group photographs; she leaves Avengers receptions early citing migraines that are, in the medical sense, real but in etiology are the somatic readout of a crowd-fear that was carved at fifteen.

## Magneto and the Brotherhood — The First False Family

The rescue. This is the foundational misfit of her psychology — the moment at which a man who would later be revealed as monstrous (and possibly her father, the canon's most unstable variable) inserted himself between her and the mob, and her body recorded the lesson: *the larger predator is the safety from the smaller predator.* The Brotherhood months that followed (*X-Men* #4 and the ambient time those issues compress) are, behaviorally, the worst kind of education: she learned to deploy her power *on command*, against people who had done her no harm, for the sake of a man she feared as much as she revered. The hex-bolts of the Brotherhood era are notably *small* — probability nudges, equipment failures, the gentle violences of someone who is being made to fight but cannot yet bring herself to *hurt*. The contrast with her later catastrophic capacity is itself diagnostic: the ceiling rose with permission. While she was under a man who demanded obedience but not enormity, the power obeyed the same limits.

Pietro's posture toward Magneto during this period — the worshipful, defensive, hair-trigger loyalty — set the second template of her enmeshment: *whatever Pietro decides about a man, I will accept until I cannot.* Her later capacity to break with Magneto is always shadowed by the period in which she could not, because her brother would not. The granular file-entry: she never spoke first at Brotherhood gatherings. She spoke only after Pietro had spoken, and only to second him, and only in a register lower than his. The voice she will use, decades later, in the early Vision marriage — soft, careful, slightly recessed — is the voice she was trained into in the Brotherhood war-room.

The first defining *choice* in her published life is the defection — *Avengers* #16, 1965, the so-called "Cap's Kooky Quartet." But the file must read it correctly. It is not, strictly, *her* choice. Pietro chose, exhausted by Magneto's escalating tyranny; she went where he went; Hawkeye's bravado provided cover; Captain America's moral authority provided a frame she could enter without having to *construct* a new self. The defection is, in the longitudinal record, the cleanest demonstration of her core early-adult pattern: *agency expressed as the selection of a new container, not as the absence of containment.* She will not stand free for years yet. What she does at Avengers Mansion is *re-bind* — to a healthier authority, in a softer hierarchy, but a hierarchy nonetheless.

## The Avengers Years — The First Re-Patterning

The early Avengers period is the first environment in which her power is *trained* rather than *deployed*. Cap's drills, Hawkeye's bickering corrections, the slow accommodation of teammates who at first read her European reserve as standoffishness and only gradually understood it as the dignity of a person who had survived being treated as an instrument. The behavioral data of this period — the era of the Kooky Quartet and the immediately following lineups — shows a young woman *learning to be looked at without being aimed*. The eye-contact pattern shifts. The shoulders begin, very gradually, to settle backward into a more upright carriage. She begins to speak first occasionally, in low-stakes contexts. She begins, in the file's most quietly important entry, *to take small pleasures* — a cup of tea brought to her by Jarvis became, in the Englehart-era flashbacks, a ritual she organized her mornings around. The capacity for *small* pleasure in a person whose early life only catalogued *large* terrors is a marker of recovery she will return to whenever she is most well.

The power itself undergoes a corresponding shift. The hex-bolts of the Avengers era are *aimed*, *titrated*, *withdrawn* on command. She can miss on purpose. She can produce effects of graduated size. She is learning, for the first time, that her capacity has a *throttle*, which is the single most important psychological discovery available to a person whose nervous system equates feeling with externality. The plateau she reached here — call it her *trained baseline* — is the level of functioning the rest of her life will be measured against, and the level she will keep trying, after every catastrophe, to climb back to.

## The Pietro Break and the Vision Choice — The First True Individuation

The Vision attachment forms slowly across the late 1960s and into the early 1970s. The clinical file should mark, with specificity, the *form* of the attraction. Vision is uncanny in exactly the way she was treated as uncanny by the mob. He is the *uncanny who is gentle*. She is, for the first time, on the *protector* side of the dyad she has only ever been the *protected* member of — and the discovery that she can offer that to someone is the most transformative input of her young adulthood. The first defining *self-initiated* choice in her record is not the defection from Magneto. It is the decision, against Pietro's loud and physically threatening opposition, to marry Vision.

The fallout is granular and lasting. Pietro's objections (*Avengers* #110, the buildup through the early Englehart issues, the climactic family-confrontation pages of *Giant-Size Avengers* #4) are not merely a brother's discomfort with his sister's partner. They are a partner-bond reacting to displacement. The twin enmeshment, articulated for the first time in language, becomes visible as the structure it always was: Pietro experienced the marriage as an infidelity, because in the years of running he had been, functionally, the only continuous love-object she had. The split with Pietro that followed the wedding — the years of cold contact, the way he would not look at Vision across briefing tables, the way she stopped speaking Romani in his presence because it was *their* private language and she could not bear what it had become — is the cost she paid for the only act of pure self-assertion of her young life.

She paid it. This is the most important data point of the Formation period. *She paid the cost and did not retract the choice.* Every later capacity she shows to hold a position against family pressure is built on the precedent of that wedding. Every later collapse back into Pietro's orbit (the *House of M* capitulation most catastrophically) is the same precedent failing under sufficient grief-load. The Vision marriage is therefore both the proof that she can individuate and the evidence of how narrow the margin of that capacity is.

## Apprenticeship Under Harkness — The First Teaching She Chose

The arrival of Agatha Harkness as instructor (*Avengers* #128 and the *Marvel Super-Heroes* #50 retrospective, the long apprenticeship of the mid-1970s) marks the first authority figure in her life *whom she chose*. Magneto chose her. The Avengers offered themselves and she accepted. Harkness she sought — or, in the more careful reading, accepted with an active "yes" that had been impossible in any prior teacher-relation. The granular behavioral shift in this period is the most positive of her young adulthood: she begins to *take notes*, the ledger habit she keeps for decades, small handwritten Romani-Latin-English hybrid notations on cards she carries folded in her coat pockets and consults under her breath before casting. The card-consultation tic, visible in late-career footage and surveillance-relevant for any operational assessment, is a Harkness-era acquisition. It is the somatic memory of being taught.

Under Harkness her power *names itself*. What had been hex — chance, probability, the language of luck — begins to be called *witchcraft*. The reframing matters psychologically: she moves from the identity of *a mutant whose mutation makes the world go wrong* to *a practitioner in a lineage*. Lineage is the thing she has never had. Her mother is unspeakable; her father is the question that wounds her; her brother is her mirror, not her line. Harkness offers her, for the first time, *a tradition to belong to that does not require her to be smaller than the room*. The Englehart-era panels in which she stands straight at the séance table and *initiates* the casting rather than waiting to be told are the visual record of a young woman beginning to inhabit her full height.

## The First Catastrophic Foreshadowing

The Formation period does not close cleanly. Embedded in it — Englehart, Mantlo, the Steve Gerber peripheries — are the seed events that the later decompensations will harvest. The first uncontrolled hex-storms during emotional crises (the marriage's early arguments produced *measurable* environmental effects — wineglasses pulsing, lamps guttering — which Vision logged with synthezoid precision and which she begged him not to mention to teammates). The first dissociative microepisode (a fugue of perhaps twenty minutes during a teaching session with Harkness, in which she "came back" holding a cup of tea she did not remember pouring, with three of Harkness's cats arranged around her feet in a precise triangle she had not consciously placed them in). The first time she said aloud — to Vision, in the privacy of their shared quarters — *I am afraid of what I can do.* All of it is in the record before the children are even conceived.

The pattern that the rest of her life will execute was complete in young adulthood: *a tender woman with a catastrophic instrument, attached too tightly to too few people, taught at last but too late, carrying an unspoken mother-wound, married to her first chosen love, and beginning — slowly, with notes and cards and small rituals and the quiet help of an old witch — to believe she might become herself.* The Formation period closes on that fragile, real, hard-won upswing. Everything that comes after is the test of whether what she built in those years can hold the weight of what is coming for it.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Spanning, in published time, the late 1970s through the late 1990s; in subject-time, the years between her wedding to the Vision and the brittle competence of the Busiek/Pérez relaunch. This is the period in which the subject acquires every adult capacity she will later have — magical discipline, marriage, motherhood, leadership — and loses each of them in turn. It is the longest stretch of her record and the one in which the patterns that detonate in 2004 are laid down, layer by layer, in plain view of anyone who knew to watch.*

---

## I. The Apprenticeship (Avengers #128 → #187; the Englehart–Mantlo–Shooter strata)

The defining structural event of this period is not the wedding. It is the moment Agatha Harkness opens her door.

Prior to Harkness, the subject's "hex" had been a folk-power: a wave of the hand, an unlikely event, an opponent tripping over a fault line of probability. The mechanism was opaque to her. She did not know what she was doing, only that she could do it, and the not-knowing was — in retrospect — a protective ignorance. Once Harkness names what she is (a witch, a practitioner of a craft with grammar, history, lineage), the subject is required for the first time in her life to *study.* The behavioral data from this period is uniformly positive: she is punctual, she is reverent, she takes notes (we see her with grimoires repeatedly, *Avengers* #147, #186), she defers without resentment to a teacher whose authority is finally not coercive. Harkness is the first older figure who asks something of her *for her own sake* rather than for a cause. The subject blooms under this.

Note the somatic register through this stretch: she carries herself differently. The headdress comes off more often; the slight forward-leaning posture of the 1960s Brotherhood pages (a girl bracing for a blow) gives way to a more squared shoulder line; her hands at rest are open rather than clasped at the chest. She begins to occupy rooms. Coulson-grade observers, were they present, would mark the shift from *frightened ward* to *young woman in possession of her own kitchen*.

But two warning patterns are already laid down in this apprenticeship period:

**First**, her practice is profoundly *teacher-anchored.* She does not, as accomplished witches of the Marvel record do, develop an independent relationship to her sources; she works *with Harkness* or, increasingly, *toward Harkness's approval.* When Harkness is later absent, withdrawn, or compromised, the subject's discipline collapses with her. The grimoires gather dust. This is not laziness. It is the same attachment dynamic that organized her childhood — *I can do the work only when a protector is in the room* — now expressed in a benign idiom.

**Second**, Harkness's central instructional doctrine — that chaos magic must be *contained, directed, and disciplined* — is taught as a craft principle. It is not taught as a *grief-management* principle. The teacher does not know, and the student does not know, that the instrument they are training is one that will eventually be required to hold a loss it cannot hold. The training prepares her to *cast.* It does not prepare her to *not cast.* In ordinary life this distinction is invisible. In the long run it is the entire ballgame.

The Korvac saga (*Avengers* #167–177, Shooter/Michelinie/Pérez, 1977–78) marks her first major test on a cosmic stage. She fights, she casts, she does not fragment. She is part of a functional team. The Avengers' near-total destruction at Korvac's hand and her own survival establish a pattern that will recur: *she absorbs the trauma of a teammate's death* (Wonder Man dies and revives across this period; Iron Man, Vision, others are reduced and restored) *without external symptomatic display.* The grief load is accumulating; the metabolic system is not yet failing.

The Trial-of-Yellowjacket / domestic-violence subplot (*Avengers* #213, Shooter, 1981) is worth noting only as observational evidence of her interpersonal style at the period's midpoint: she takes Janet's side instantly, physically present at her friend's apartment, brings food, does not press for narrative. She is, with women in pain, *good.* This will remain true across the entire record.

---

## II. The West Coast Years — The First True Adulthood (Avengers West Coast #1 → #50)

The Englehart-driven *West Coast Avengers* (1984–88) is the period that retrospective surveillance reads with the most aching attention, because it is the only stretch of the subject's life in which she is, by any ordinary measure, *happy in a sustainable way.*

She and Vision relocate to the Compound. She decorates. (The interior set-dressing across these issues is consistent: warm earth tones, fabric over hard surfaces, candles, a small herb garden Vision waters with elaborate care — domestic markers of a woman who is finally, deliberately, building a *room* of her own.) She maintains the Harkness study schedule. She is on the active roster but rotates off when her chairmanship of the team is not required; she chooses, repeatedly, the smaller domestic obligation over the larger field deployment. The defining behavioral marker of this period: *she puts the home first, on purpose, and is not ashamed of it.* Read against her later self-loathing as "destroyer," this stretch is the photographic negative.

The pseudo-pregnancies (*Vision and the Scarlet Witch* vol. 2, #3, Englehart/Leonardi, 1985–86) arrive within this domestic frame as the apparent fulfillment of it. The pregnancy is, from her sensorium, *real:* morning sickness, weight, fetal movement, the bone-deep biological time of carrying. Harkness intervenes obstetrically (a fact that the subject experiences as motherly attention from her own elder-mother figure). The births of Thomas and William are presented to her, to Vision, and to her chosen kin as the births of children. She nurses. She wakes at night. She names them. She *parents* — and the data of her parenting, across the two years between births and erasure, is uniformly consistent with a competent, doting, slightly anxious first-time mother who is supported by an unusually patient partner.

The covert physiological fact — that the children's substrate is Mephisto's soul-fragmentation, drawn into form by the subject's unrecognized reality-shaping capacity — is invisible to her. This invisibility is the pivot of everything that follows. *She is not constructing a fantasy. She is, from her own vantage, raising her sons.* When the construct collapses, the loss will not be the loss of a fantasy. It will be the loss of two children. Any clinical reading that treats the wound otherwise is reading it wrong.

The Englehart departure mid-run (an editorial event invisible to the subject but consequential to her record) is followed by the Byrne arrival (*WCA* #42–57, 1988–89), and with Byrne the world the subject has carefully built is dismantled, deliberately and methodically, in roughly eighteen issues.

---

## III. Vision Quest and Darker Than Scarlet — The First True Decompensation (WCA #42–57)

The dismantling proceeds in a precise order, and the order matters because it isolates each defense she has built and removes it before the next is removed.

**Phase one: the husband.** Vision is seized by a covert international taskforce, disassembled to component parts, and reassembled as a colorless, affectless construct who does not remember the marriage as the marriage was. The subject's first response is *not* collapse. It is fury and competence: she finds him, she retrieves him, she insists on the rebuild. The behavioral data here is critical — *under acute, identifiable threat to a loved object, she mobilizes effectively.* She is not a fragile person in a crisis. She is a fragile person in an *unmetabolized* crisis. The distinction will become diagnostic.

When the reassembled Vision proves incapable of returning to who he was — when she discovers that the man she married is, functionally, not coming back — her response shifts. She withdraws into the Compound. She speaks less. She holds the white Vision's hand in public and is observed (Hawkeye's eyeline, Tigra's worried sidelong) to flinch slightly from his touch in private. The somatic record: she begins to sleep less, eat irregularly, lose weight; the hex-bolts she throws in training exercises during this stretch are noted by teammates as "wilder," undershooting and overshooting targets she had hit reliably for years. Affect-power coupling is already destabilizing.

**Phase two: the children.** Harkness — and the editorial decision behind her — chooses this moment to inform the subject that the children are not children, that they were soul-fragments, that they have been reabsorbed by their original substrate, and that the subject will be best served by *forgetting them.* The memory-wipe is performed with the subject's nominal consent under conditions in which she has no resources to refuse. The intervention is, by any clinical analog, a catastrophic boundary violation by a trusted figure: a therapist excising rather than treating a wound. The subject — having lost the children twice now, once to revelation and once to erasure — walks back into the Compound *without consciously remembering she has lost anything,* and the unconscious holds the entire weight.

This is the moment after which she is, structurally, sick. Every subsequent decompensation is the system trying and failing to bear what was put into it on this day.

**Phase three: the agency violations.** Magneto re-enters the record in this window (*Avengers West Coast* #56–62, "Darker Than Scarlet"), in collaboration — chosen or coerced is contested in the text — with Immortus. The subject is taken, mind-influenced, dressed in the period's "Darker Than Scarlet" costume (a visual cue the surveillance file should mark: she costumes-up *darkly* every time her agency is being violated; the body and the wardrobe both signal the dissociation), and used as an instrument. Her behavioral display through these issues is *visibly dissociated:* she speaks in shorter sentences, her affective range narrows to a flat smile or a flat rage, she does not weep, she does not flinch. This is not the woman who left the Compound. This is what is left of her when the Compound is gone, the husband is gone, the children are gone (consciously) or unbearable (unconsciously), and a father-figure is once again telling her what she is for.

The Avengers extract her. The mind-control is broken. The behavioral aftermath, across the early 1990s, is the *brittle stability* the shared workup names. Worth specifying further:

She returns to active duty quickly — too quickly, by any clinical standard. She does not take leave. She does not seek therapeutic intervention (Harkness, the figure to whom she would in better times turn, is now structurally implicated in the wound). She *covers.* She runs the line. She is competent in the field. Her teammates note that she "seems herself again." She is not herself again. She is a high-functioning post-traumatic adaptation impersonating herself, and the impersonation will hold for roughly thirteen years.

---

## IV. The Long Recovery That Was Not a Recovery (1990–1998)

Across the Roy/Dann Thomas, the Harras, and the early-Busiek-adjacent stretches of the Avengers' main and West Coast titles, the subject occupies a peculiar narrative position: *present but rarely centered.* She fights every major event (the Crossing, Operation: Galactic Storm, Bloodties, the Infinity sequences peripheral to her own arc), she sustains the team's emotional middle, she is reliable. She is not the subject of an arc of her own for nearly a decade.

What the surveillance file should record about this period is precisely what the published record makes hard to see: *what she does between panels.*

**Wonder Man.** Her romance with Simon Williams (developed across *Avengers* #312 onward and threading through the 1990s) is, behaviorally, an *anti-Vision* choice and simultaneously a *Vision-substitute* choice. Simon is warm where Vision was cool, embodied where Vision was constructed, mortal-presenting where Vision was synthetic — but he is also, critically, *ionic-energy-immortal,* hard to kill in the ordinary way, and (after his first death) returnable. The unconscious specification has not changed: *I will love only what cannot leave the way ordinary people leave.* The complication that Vision's brain patterns were originally derived from Simon's gives the relationship a *somatic eeriness* the subject does not name aloud but is observed to register — she touches Simon's face sometimes with a small startled pause, then continues. The relationship is not unhappy. It is also not the relationship she had. She does not marry him. She does not move in. She maintains a quarters of her own at every iteration of Avengers Mansion across this stretch — *she does not nest again.*

**Pietro.** The twin re-enters the picture more frequently across this period in his X-Factor role and his Inhuman royal-consort role (Crystal, Luna). The subject is observed to schedule trips around his location, to fly to Attilan, to spend long stretches with her infant niece. Crystal's eventual infidelity and Pietro's collapse pulls the subject toward him repeatedly; she is the family-mediator in every public-record dispute. Note that her own grief is at this point fully sublimated; she is available to *Pietro's* grief in a way she does not allow herself to be available to her own. This caretaking is, observationally, a defense — the role of supporter spares her the role of sufferer.

**Magneto.** The paternity revelation (*Vision and the Scarlet Witch* vol. 2 #4 onward) sits in this period as a still-unresolved structural fact. The subject is observed across the 1990s to *not visit* him, to *not mention* him spontaneously, and yet to respond instantly and with full mobilization whenever a Magneto-event breaks (Bloodties, *Fatal Attractions*, the X-Men/Avengers crossovers). She positions herself between Magneto and the Avengers' more punitive members reflexively. She does not call him father. She also does not allow him to be destroyed. The behavior is consistent with an avoidant relationship to an unresolvable attachment — *I cannot bear his presence; I cannot bear his absence.*

**Harkness.** Largely off-screen across this stretch, by Harkness's own withdrawal. The subject does not, in the surveillance record, seek her out. The reasons can only be inferred: at some pre-conscious level the subject knows Harkness took something from her, and the not-knowing-what produces a relational chill she cannot explain.

**Practice.** Her magical work plateaus and, in places, regresses. Without Harkness, without active study, her hexes return toward the folk-power register of her earliest career. She handles this competently in public and almost certainly with private frustration; the *Force Works* era (a brief Iron Man-led splinter team, 1994–96) shows her power-output increasingly volatile, sometimes oversized, sometimes failing, with no clear pattern other than affective. The coupling is reasserting itself. Nobody on the team — Stark included — diagnoses it.

**Somatic markers across this stretch:** sleep irregular; the small habits of an under-resourced person accumulate. She is observed to drink coffee constantly in Mansion scenes. She develops a habit of pressing her palm flat against any vertical surface (a wall, a doorframe) when entering a new room — a small grounding gesture that observers in 1968 photographs do not show. She wears her hair forward more, partially covering the face. She laughs less; when she laughs, she laughs fully. She is *kind* without interruption — even in dispute, even in field combat against former friends, the kindness does not leave. This is the most important compensatory datum of the period: *the niceness survives the damage.* It is not performance. It is structural.

**The Crossing and the Onslaught break-and-rebuild (1995–96).** She loses teammates (the Wasp, Captain America, the original lineup) to apparent deaths during Onslaught; she helps reconstitute the team after. The data is consistent: in collective catastrophe she is present, useful, and tearful in the appropriate degree. In private catastrophe she is fragmenting. The 1990s Avengers had no instrument for noticing the second condition under the cover of the first.

---

## V. Heroes Return — The Performance of Wholeness (Avengers vol. 3 #1 → #56; Busiek/Pérez, 1998–2002)

The Busiek/Pérez relaunch presents the subject at what looks, on the page, like a full reintegration. She is in costume. She is on the line. She is dating Simon (and, in private subtext, drawn toward the reassembled Vision again — the triangulation across these issues is one of the subtlest emotional plotlines in the run and behaviorally one of the most diagnostic). She is on the founding active roster. She is, when Cap is absent or Iron Man is dealing with his own crises, the *moral spine* of the team in many issues — the voice that says *we do not do that to prisoners,* the voice that argues for the Squadron Supreme's autonomy in the Kang War's prologue, the voice that goes to the bedside of the wounded.

She is also, by every quiet metric, *hollower than she has ever been.*

The behavioral specifics:

She practices magic *more* in this period than she has since the Englehart years — but the practice is undirected. She studies in her quarters at night, alone, without a teacher. The runes pile up. She is reaching for something she cannot name. The power is intensifying (Busiek and Pérez visibly escalate the scale of her castings across the run — a hex that derails a Kang battalion in #43 is several orders larger than anything from her 1970s register), and the subject is herself uneasy about the escalation. She mentions to Simon, in one quiet scene, that her "control feels different now." He treats it as ordinary intimate disclosure. It is, by the standards of any competent monitor of her case, a *prodrome.*

She returns to Vision, briefly and incompletely. The reconciliation does not stabilize either of them. The triangulation with Simon collapses both relationships toward stalled friendships. By the run's late stretches she is, romantically, alone. Surveillance note: she does not seem to mourn this. The flatness with which she absorbs the end of both relationships is itself the data — *she has run out of metabolic capacity for ordinary losses.*

The Kang War (*Avengers* #41–55) is her last fully-functional field deployment of the period. She fights brilliantly. She mourns the dead competently. She returns to Mansion. She closes her door.

The final issues of the Busiek run, and the early-Geoff-Johns transitional stretch, show a woman whose behavior has narrowed: she trains, she eats alone, she practices magic alone, she does not initiate conversations, she responds graciously to those initiated with her. The pastoral domesticity of the West Coast Compound is now nearly twenty years gone and has not been replaced. The children are not consciously remembered. The husband is, in some sense, not consciously *lost* either, because the loss was never permitted to complete.

The system is loaded to capacity. The detonation in 2004 is not a surprise to anyone who has read the file. It is the predictable expression of a wound that was never allowed to drain, in an instrument that converts wound directly into world.

---

## VI. Pattern Summary of the Middle Period

What the long middle of the subject's life establishes, for the file:

1. **She can be taught.** Under a competent, affectionate teacher she acquires discipline rapidly and uses it well. The implication, prospectively, is that the late-period mentorship work she eventually undertakes is not a departure from her nature but a return to its best stretch.

2. **She can build a home.** The West Coast Compound years are proof of concept. *She knows how to nest.* The loss of the home and the failure to rebuild it for nearly two decades afterward is not preference; it is wound.

3. **She mobilizes brilliantly in identifiable crisis and collapses slowly in ambient grief.** The diagnostic implication is precise: she needs adversaries she can *see,* not adversaries that are *time.* Grief, which is the adversary that is time, is the one she cannot fight.

4. **Her power tracks her affect more tightly with every decade.** The coupling intensifies. By the end of this period the buffer between *feeling* and *manifesting* is functionally gone. Any therapeutic intervention not designed around this fact will fail. (Harkness's failed.)

5. **Iatrogenic injury is the single largest accelerant in her record.** More damaging than Magneto's coercion, more damaging than the children's loss as such, is the *erasure* of the children's loss. Any future caretaker should be marked, in red, on the principle: *do not edit her memory. Do not edit her perception. Do not tell her that what she felt was not what happened. The thing she cannot survive is being told that her reality is wrong.*

6. **The kindness is structural and does not erode.** This is the file's most important positive datum across the entire middle period. Under every iteration of stress, the subject's default toward the wounded, the marginalized, the frightened, and the small remains intact. Whatever else she becomes when the system finally fails, she does not become cruel. This will matter, prospectively, when the system fails.

The middle period ends with the subject standing alone in a quiet room in a rebuilt Mansion, practicing a craft she half-remembers, loved by people who do not know what she has lost, holding — without knowing she is holding — the entire weight of a grief that was placed in her and sealed there by a teacher she trusted, two decades before. What happens next is not her fault in the sense the world will later assign. It is, however, *predictable* — and the predictability is what the file exists to record.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## Frame and Boundary of "Recent"

For dossier purposes, "recent" begins with her death and resurrection in the *Trial of Magneto* sequence (2021) and runs forward through the Orlando solo (*Scarlet Witch* vol. 3, 2023–24; *Scarlet Witch & Quicksilver*, 2024), the *Contest of Chaos* summer crossover (2023), her tenure rotating through *Avengers* (Jed MacKay, 2023–) and the X-line's *Fall of X / From the Ashes* aftershocks, the *Blood Hunt* vampire incursion (2024), and into present operational status. The frame matters because it brackets the most psychologically significant stretch of her recorded life: the first sustained period in which she is *neither* in catastrophic decompensation *nor* in dissociative refuge. She is, for the first time across sixty years of file, *consistently present in her own life.*

---

## 1. The *Trial of Magneto* Hinge (2021–22) — Death, Return, and the Forced Speaking of the Names

The hinge event of the recent period is the murder-and-resurrection sequence opening Aaron's late *Avengers* arc and continuing through *X-Men: Trial of Magneto* (Williams/Yıldırım). Subject is found dead on Krakoa, body posed like a martyr; the X-line spends five issues litigating who killed her. The eventual revelation — that *she killed herself* via a contingent magical trap, engineered with the foreknowledge that her resurrection would force the X-line to formally acknowledge Wiccan and Speed as her children — is one of the most diagnostically important acts in her file.

Read the structure: she weaponized her own death not as suicide-by-despair (the prior decompensations) but as *deliberate ritual* — a planned, instrumental, *forward-facing* act whose purpose was to compel the world to speak two names it had spent fifteen years refusing to speak. This is the first time in her record that her omnipotent-reparative drive is harnessed *through* her grief rather than *around* it. She does not rewrite the world; she stages a piece of theater the world cannot look away from. The result: Billy Kaplan / Wiccan is formally restored to her, mother-and-son reunion is canonized, and the public record now lists her as parent.

Behavioral data from the resurrection sequence: she emerges quieter than at any prior return. Hair shorn shorter for several issues (a self-presentation shift that, in surveillance terms, signals a deliberate break with the prior body-image); slower cadence in dialogue; demonstrably reduced hex-discharge in moments of stress (a pencil-tic in the art: hands stay still where in prior eras they would already be glowing). This is *behavioral self-regulation appearing for the first time at baseline.*

She declines, in the immediate aftermath, to rejoin any team. The declination is itself the data — for sixty years she has answered grief by attaching to a protective frame. Here she chooses solitude. Not the dissociative solitude of the *Children's Crusade* fugues (hiding in pastoral domesticity, amnesiac), but *elected* solitude with intent: she rents an apartment above an occult shop in New York's Lower East Side ("the Emporium," per Orlando), opens a door to walk-in clients, and begins the work the file has been waiting decades for her to do.

---

## 2. The Emporium Period (Orlando *Scarlet Witch* vol. 3, 2023–24) — The Adaptive Reorganization

The Orlando solo run is, for dossier purposes, the **single richest behavioral dataset** on subject in the modern era. It documents her at a granularity prior eras never permitted: not as Avenger-on-mission or Avenger-in-crisis but as *resident, neighbor, employer, mentor, sleeper, eater, walker.* Every panel is forensic material.

**Residence and ecology.** Above-shop walk-up, Lower East Side. Door is a *literal* magical door — anyone in genuine need can find it, no appointment, no vetting. The choice is diagnostic: she is constructing a frame in which she *cannot* refuse the wounded who present, which both (a) institutionalizes her reparative drive in a sustainable channel and (b) ensures she is never alone with her own thoughts for long. The defense is now *adaptive* — the same omnipotent-reparation drive that built the constructed children and the *House of M* world is now metered out into daily, retail-scale interventions.

**Daily rhythm (inferable).** Shop opens late morning; she is observed making coffee in a small kitchen above the floor; she keeps a chalkboard inventory in script that mixes English, Romani diacritics, and Latin sigils; she eats sparingly during work hours but takes proper meals after closing, usually alone or with the apprentice.
