The phenomenon is *passive* — she is not casting; she is *bleeding*. Observers in proximity to her during heavy grief states should expect low-grade reality-fray in a roughly six-meter radius. This is the early-warning signature for catastrophic decompensation, the small precursor to the large.

**The trapdoor.** Under specific compounding conditions — grief plus agency-violation plus exhaustion plus the presence of someone telling her her perception is wrong — the entire defense structure collapses and the omnipotent-reparative mechanism engages. The *House of M* and *Disassembled* breaks both followed this exact compound. The trapdoor is *not* opened by grief alone, nor by stress alone, nor by threat alone; it requires the specific combination. Surveillance and care protocols must monitor for the combination, not for the components.

---

## VII. VICTORY — AN UNFAMILIAR STATE

Victory does not produce in her the behaviors victory produces in most operators; she does not exult, does not celebrate easily, does not accept congratulation gracefully.

**Immediate post-victory.** A long exhale, the aura receding, and then a specific small behavior: she will look for the people on her team and physically locate each one, often touching a shoulder or the back of a hand. The accounting is unconscious and consistent. Only after the accounting is complete does she allow her own posture to relax.

**Public acknowledgment.** She accepts thanks with a small nod and a deflection ("we all did" or the equivalent). She does not enjoy ceremony and will leave any ceremony at the earliest courteous moment. Photographs catch her looking sideways, looking down, looking away — she does not pose easily and has not learned to.

**Private post-victory.** The melancholic baseline returns quickly, sometimes within the hour. Companions report that she becomes *sadder* after a victory than before, which is correct: victories remind her of the victories that were not won — Vision not saved, the children not kept, the mutants not spared. *Every victory is haunted by the catalog of defeats it does not undo.* She knows this about herself and does not fight it; she takes a long bath, she reads, she goes to bed early, she begins again the next day.

**The exception.** Apprentice success — an apprentice landing a spell, a dependent crossing a threshold of competence or healing — produces in her the only documented unguarded joy in the record. She *laughs*, audibly, and her face transforms. The eye-smile is full. She will embrace the apprentice without hesitation. This is the cleanest indicator available of where her best self lives.

---

## VIII. DEFEAT — THE CHARACTERISTIC RESPONSE

**Tactical defeat (a fight lost, a plan failed, a mission incomplete).** Stoic, brief withdrawal, accountability-taking. She will articulate her own errors before others articulate them and absorb blame slightly in excess of her share. She does not externalize. She does not blame teammates. She returns to function within a day.

**Personal defeat (a relationship ending, an apprentice failing, a loved one wounded).** This goes deeper. She withdraws to a domestic frame — a small house, a country place, a borrowed room — and *cleans*. The cleaning is methodical and ritual: she will wash floors, mend cloth, organize small objects, for hours. The behavior is reparative-displaced; she cannot fix what is broken so she fixes what she can. Companions who know her will sit with her during the cleaning without commenting on it; this is the correct intervention.

**Catastrophic defeat (a death she could not prevent, particularly of a dependent).** The most dangerous category. Here the early-warning signatures — the bleeding into reality, the throat-flush, the murmured Romani, the hand to the abdomen — all surge together. She will isolate; isolation is the wrong intervention. The historically correct intervention is the presence of a trusted figure (Steve Rogers, Strange, Wiccan, Pietro at his best) who does not try to fix and does not try to talk her out of the grief, but who *occupies the room* and prevents the trapdoor combination from assembling. Without such presence, the omnipotent-reparative break becomes available.

**Self-defeat (the recognition that she has herself caused harm).** This is the deepest wound and produces the most paradoxical behavior. She becomes *more functional*, not less — she takes on penance work, she serves, she gives, she shows up early and stays late. The shame-saturated self-concept (§3) drives a reparative overcompensation that looks externally like heroism and is internally like flagellation. The late-period solo work and the *Trial of Magneto* return-to-life arcs both express this pattern. It is *adaptive* in its outputs and *unhealed* in its source. Treatment requires interrupting the penance frame with the


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# Daily Life, Routines & Rituals — Subject: Wanda Maximoff

*A week of dedicated surveillance on the subject does not yield the choreography of a typical young woman in her twenties. It yields the choreography of a convalescent — someone organizing her hours around the prevention of relapse. What follows is the granular pattern reconstructed from sustained observation across her stable periods (the late solo-run intervals, the post–Trial of Magneto reintegration, the quiet stretches between catastrophes). The shape of her day is the shape of her therapy.*

---

## 1. The Architecture of a Day

### 1.1 Pre-dawn / The Waking

The subject wakes early and badly. Observation logs across multiple lodgings — the brownstone apartment of the solo period, the rooms at Avengers Mountain, the temporary safehouses, the cottages she is drawn to in the rural interludes — converge on a window between **04:40 and 05:30**. The waking is rarely clean. Audio captures, when available, record a short intake of breath, sometimes a single whispered word (most often a name; the names recur and are known), and a delay of forty to ninety seconds before any motion. She does not reach for a phone. She does not turn on a light.

The first physical act is almost invariably the same: she sits up, plants both feet flat on the floor, and presses her palms downward against the mattress on either side of her thighs. Surveillance interprets this as a grounding maneuver — a learned somatic exercise consistent with trauma-focused therapy protocols. The palms-flat-down posture is held for thirty to sixty seconds. Only then does she stand.

She drinks water before anything else. A glass kept on the bedside table the night before, room-temperature, finished in two or three swallows. The glass is then placed — not set down distractedly, but *placed* — at a consistent location on the nightstand. The orderliness of small objects in her immediate sphere is a constant; the orderliness of her larger world is not.

### 1.2 First Hour — The Threshold Rituals

Between the waking and any contact with another human being or device, there is a protected interval of roughly forty-five to seventy-five minutes. This interval contains, in observed sequence:

- **Stillness work.** She sits, usually on the floor, often on a folded shawl or a small rug, back against a wall or a piece of furniture (never freestanding — she requires the contact). Eyes closed or half-closed. Breathing audible but unforced. Duration: fifteen to thirty minutes. This is *not* formal meditation in the lotus-and-mala sense; it is closer to what trauma clinicians call *interoceptive monitoring* — checking the body for what is present before the day can write over it. The hands are usually kept open, palms up, on her knees. When her power is active or unsettled, a faint reddish lensing of the air is visible at her fingertips; she has been observed to look down at it without alarm and wait for it to subside before continuing.

- **A short verbal ritual.** Lip-reading and intermittent audio capture indicate that she speaks, very quietly, what appears to be a private litany. The full text is not recoverable. Recurring fragments include the names of the dead, the names of the living she loves, and — repeatedly — the phrase *"I am here, today is today."* The litany is not religious in form, though it borrows the cadence of one. It functions as a daily reality-anchor.

- **Coffee or strong tea.** Coffee in the American interludes; black tea, very strong, when she is in Europe or in any cottage-phase. Prepared by hand — a small stovetop pot, a kettle. No automated machines in any lodging she has chosen herself. Coffee taken with a small amount of milk; tea taken without. Sweetened only when she is unwell, and then heavily.

- **The window.** Whatever the lodging, she goes to a window within the first hour and stands at it for two to five minutes. Surveillance has not identified a religious or magical function. It appears to be checking — establishing where she is, what the weather is, whether the light is the light she expects.

### 1.3 Mid-Morning — The Work

The character of her work hours has changed across eras, but the *shape* of the work block is stable: **roughly 08:00 to 12:30**, with one break at the midpoint.

In her solo-practice periods, this block is given to *casework* — the witches, the haunted persons, the small magical injuries she has taken on as her practice. She handles them in a manner more reminiscent of a country doctor than a sorcerer: she sits with the petitioner, she listens at length before she acts, she takes handwritten notes (she keeps notebooks; see §3.4), she asks unhurried questions about sleep and appetite and family, and she touches the person — usually a hand on a forearm or shoulder — at a moment chosen with care. The magical intervention, when it comes, is short and quiet. She does not perform. The "casting" most often looks like nothing at all from the outside: a steadying of breath, a flicker of red at the fingertips, the petitioner blinking and looking better.

In her Avengers-active periods, the morning block is given to briefings, training, and the maintenance work of a team member who knows she is on probation in the eyes of most teammates. She arrives to briefings *early* — five to ten minutes before the scheduled time — and chooses the same seat each time when she can: against a wall, sightline on the door, never in the center of the room. She listens more than she speaks. When she does speak in a tactical meeting, she speaks last, after the room has shaped a consensus, and her contributions are most often *corrective* in a quiet register — *"That building has a daycare on the second floor,"* or *"He is afraid, not angry. We can use that."*

In both eras, she takes a single break in the late morning, usually around **10:30**, and the break is almost always *outdoors*. A walk around a block. A stand on a balcony. A few minutes in a courtyard. She does not take coffee breaks indoors with colleagues; she takes air breaks alone.

### 1.4 Midday — The Meal and the Pause

She eats lunch. This is worth noting because in her decompensated periods she does not, and the surveillance value of *whether she eats lunch* as a daily wellness indicator is high.

The meal is small, savory, and warm when it can be. Soup, eggs, a small plate of vegetables and grain, occasionally fish. She prepares it herself when she can, takes it standing at a counter or sitting at a small table, and tends to eat slowly with long pauses. She does not eat while reading, while working, or while looking at a screen — the eating is its own activity. If forced to eat at a working lunch, she becomes quieter and eats less.

After lunch she rests, briefly. Twenty to forty minutes. Not always sleep — sometimes a chair and a book, sometimes lying flat on a couch with one arm across her eyes, sometimes the floor again. The rest is non-negotiable in periods of stability. Its absence is an early indicator of relapse risk.

### 1.5 Afternoon — The Second Work Block

**13:30 to roughly 17:30.** This is the block in which she does the heavier or more outward-facing work — fieldwork, travel, magical operations that require setup, longer apprentice sessions, calls and visits she has been putting off. The afternoon block is where the public-facing Scarlet Witch operates, when she operates publicly. Combat and confrontation, when it falls into her week, falls almost always into this block; her body and her power are most regulated and most coordinated between roughly **14:00 and 17:00**, and she has plainly learned this about herself.

A consistent sub-pattern: **she takes apprentices seriously, and they get her best hours.** When a younger witch, mentee, or — in the relevant periods — Wiccan or Speed is in her orbit, the afternoon block reorients around them. She asks them what they have practiced. She watches them work and corrects them in a low voice. She is patient in a way that observers used to her catastrophic register find startling.

### 1.6 Evening — The Soft Hours

The hours between roughly **17:30 and 21:00** are the most domestic and the most *chosen* of her day. They are also the hours of greatest variability across eras, but the variations are themselves patterned:

- **Cooking.** When she is in a stable phase and has a kitchen, she cooks. Slowly, with attention. Eastern European dishes from the half-remembered childhood (a paprika-heavy stew, a cabbage dish, a yeasted bread) appear in a rotation with the foods of whatever city she is currently in. She has been observed to cook for one with the same care she cooks for guests; in the cottage periods she has cooked for one for weeks at a stretch.

- **Reading.** Heavy in her schedule. Fiction (she favors novels with strong family structures and unhurried interior lives), poetry (her shelves consistently hold work by women writers in translation — Akhmatova, Szymborska, Tsvetaeva recur), and a working library of occult and folkloric texts that she treats as *reference*, not as entertainment. She marks books with small slips of paper, never with marginalia in pen; underlinings, when they appear, are in pencil and very light.

- **Music.** Played quietly. Wide-ranging, but the recurring picks lean toward voices — older recordings of European folk singers, contemporary singer-songwriters with restrained arrangements, occasional liturgical music (not from her own tradition; she listens *across*). Surveillance audio rarely captures anything loud. She has been observed to sit with a single song on repeat for an hour at a time during low periods.

- **Long calls.** A small number of phone or comm-line contacts receive a long evening call once or twice a week. The list is short and stable: her brother (calls highly variable in temperature, sometimes ending abruptly, almost always resumed within forty-eight hours), her sons in the eras when they are in contact, one or two of the Avengers she trusts personally rather than tactically, a small constellation of witches in her practice network. She does not text small talk. She writes long, careful messages or she calls.

### 1.7 Night — The Threshold Back

Bedtime drifts later than is healthy for her — typically **23:30 to 01:00.** She knows this and has spoken of it in fragments to apprentices. The lateness is defensive: *sleep is when the unbidden comes.*

The pre-sleep ritual is as patterned as the morning's. She washes her face — slowly, with cool water, both hands flat. She brushes her hair, always at least fifty strokes (this is not vanity; it is rhythm). She lays out the next day's clothing in a specific order on a chair or a hook. She refills the bedside water glass. She closes — physically closes — any open books and aligns them.

In bed, she reads for ten to thirty minutes, then turns off the light and lies on her back with her hands folded on her sternum for the first stretch. She tends to fall asleep on her left side, knees drawn slightly up, the bedding pulled to the shoulder. Sleep is achieved within fifteen to forty minutes in stable periods. In unstable periods she sometimes does not sleep until the small hours, and surveillance has recorded her sitting up at three or four in the morning at a window with a cup of tea long gone cold.

---

## 2. The Weekly Shape

A surveillance week on the subject reveals a *rhythm of expansion and contraction* — outward-facing days alternating with inward-facing days, in a roughly two-to-one ratio.

- **Outward days** (typically three to four per week): work block with petitioners or teammates, afternoon fieldwork, evening contact with one or two people. She is visible, audible, present in the world.
- **Inward days** (typically two to three per week): the architecture above runs but with no external contact. She does not leave the lodging for more than a walk. She cooks for one. She reads. She practices alone. These are not depressive days — they are *maintenance* days. She has learned that she needs them.
- **One day of near-total stillness per week**, usually but not always at the weekend's edge. On this day even the casework is suspended. She has described this in passing as "a sabbath that isn't one." It is a non-negotiable.

The two-to-one ratio inverts during periods of stress — more inward days, fewer outward. A surveillance signal of approaching relapse is the *disappearance of outward days altogether for more than five consecutive days*, which historically precedes withdrawal into pastoral hideaways and longer dissociative episodes.

### 2.1 Anniversaries

The calendar contains marked dates. Surveillance correlation across years confirms that on certain days the entire routine compresses and goes silent:

- **The day she lost Vision** (the original dismantling, and its successor losses): a day spent largely alone, often with extended candlelit stillness in the evening. She does not work that day. She does not see petitioners. She does not answer non-urgent calls.
- **The day the children were taken from her memory** (and the surrounding calendrical cluster): the most fragile day of her year. She has been observed to travel to be near her sons on or around this date in the eras when they are accessible; in eras when they are not, she has been observed to construct a small private observance — two place settings at a table, two candles, a long sit.
- **Her mother's death date** (as reconstructed): a day of cooking. Specifically, the foods she associates with the figure of the mother. Eating alone, slowly.
- **Pietro's birthday — which is her own.** The most behaviorally complex day of the year. She and her brother almost always make contact; the contact ranges from a long warm evening to a single contested call that ends in silence. Surveillance treats this day as *high-volatility, low-risk* — emotionally intense, but rarely catalytic.

---

## 3. Habits of Place, Object, and Body

### 3.1 Habits of Place

She is **strongly territorial in small ways and weakly territorial in large ones.** She does not insist on a particular city or country — across her record she has lived in New York, in a series of European cities, in rural cottages on three continents, in shared team residences. But within whatever space she occupies, she rapidly establishes:

- **A chair.** Her chair. Visitors learn quickly not to sit in it. In communal residences she has been observed to mark her chair subtly — a folded shawl across the back, a book on the seat, a cup on the side table — and to feel its violation when another teammate displaces it.
- **A corner for practice.** Even in transient lodgings, a small area is set up for stillness work and any magical operation that requires preparation. Surveillance has documented the consistent contents: a folded textile to sit on (often dark red, occasionally embroidered), a small dish (used for water, salt, or ash depending on the working), one or two candles, a small object she has carried for a long time (variously described — a coin, a worn cloth, a piece of jewelry; she does not display it).
- **A window she uses.** See §1.2. In any lodging, within the first day, she identifies a window and that window becomes hers.

In open or public spaces she is reliably *back-to-wall, sightline-to-exit.* In restaurants, on benches, in transit, the pattern holds. She does not appear to notice she is doing it.

### 3.2 Habits of Dress

The crimson is for work, not for life. In daily wear she favors:

- Long sleeves regardless of weather. (Observation: she touches her own forearms frequently when thinking, a small self-soothing gesture; the sleeves are functional to that habit.)
- Dark colors, with the auburn-and-red palette appearing in small accents — a scarf, a lining, an inner garment, a piece of jewelry. The red is *always present somewhere* on her person, even on her quietest days. Surveillance interprets this as identity-anchoring rather than ostentation.
- Soft textiles. Wools, knits, washed linens. Nothing stiff. Nothing that constrains the chest or the throat.
- A consistent set of small jewelry. Earrings she does not change often. One or two rings that move between hands and fingers depending on what she is doing. (The ring movement is itself a tell — see §3.5.)
- Footwear chosen for *quiet*. Soft-soled boots in winter, soft shoes in summer. She walks almost silently in any lodging.

Hair is worn down most often; pulled back loosely when she is working with her hands, in a single low gathering at the nape when she is in the field. She brushes it herself, every night, and does not let others touch it casually.

### 3.3 Habits of Eating and Drinking

- **Coffee in the morning, tea through the day, water always within reach.** She is rarely without a cup near her.
- **Eats small portions slowly.** Will leave food on a plate. Does not finish out of politeness.
- **Cooks more than she eats out.** When she does eat out, she favors small, quiet, family-run places. She tips well and consistently and tends to return to the same establishment until something disturbs the routine.
- **Alcohol is occasional and ceremonial.** A glass of wine with a meal in company. She is not observed drinking alone in stable periods. In unstable periods she does not drink at all — surveillance reads this as a deliberate abstention; she will not introduce another disinhibitor into a system already prone to overflow.
- **Bread.** She bakes it when she has a kitchen. The smell of yeast in her lodging is a high-confidence indicator of a stable week.

### 3.4 Habits of Recording

She **writes by hand**, daily, in small notebooks. Surveillance has identified at least three concurrent notebooks at any given time:

1. **A casework notebook** — notes on petitioners, workings attempted, outcomes. Kept in a careful, almost clinical hand.
2. **A personal notebook** — looser, sometimes a journal entry, sometimes a list, sometimes a drawing. The drawings are observed to be predominantly of hands, of windows, and of two small figures rendered without faces.
3. **A book of names** — a long, ongoing list of the people she has lost and the people she has wounded. She adds to it. She does not, observably, cross anything out.

She does not keep digital journals. Her digital footprint is, by the standards of someone in her cohort, *unusually small* — minimal social media presence, no public-facing personal accounts, a single secured comm-line for team and one or two for personal contact. This is not technophobia; it is the discipline of someone whose interiority has been used against her and against the world.

### 3.5 Habits of the Body — The Micro-Tells

A surveillance file of the subject's body across a week records the following recurring micro-patterns:

- **Palms pressed flat downward** against any available surface — bed, floor, table, thigh — at moments of emotional load. This is the most diagnostic somatic gesture. The frequency and duration of palm-pressing across a day is a near-real-time index of her affective state. *Increased palm-pressing precedes every documented episode of significant power-output variance.*
- **Touching her own forearms** through her sleeves when listening, thinking, or hearing something painful. A wrapping-of-self gesture.
- **The ring-shift.** She wears one to three rings; under stress she rotates a ring on its finger, or moves a ring from one hand to the other. The faster the movement, the higher the load.
- **A short pause before speech** in any high-stakes conversation. Not hesitation in the uncertain sense; rather, a small reset. Lip-readers report the pause is sometimes filled by the same single inaudible breath-word, the meaning of which is not securely identified.
- **Eye-contact pattern.** Steady and warm with a single interlocutor; flickers away in groups; drops to the middle distance when the topic approaches the children, Vision, Magneto, or the events of the major decompensations. The middle-distance gaze is a high-confidence indicator that the conversation has crossed into territory she cannot, in that moment, safely hold.
- **The hand-glow.** Faint red lensing at the fingertips. Most often invisible to casual observation, requiring close optics or low-light conditions to register. *Continuous low-level glow* is her resting state in periods of magical engagement and is not concerning. *Flickering, asymmetric, or pulsing glow* indicates dysregulation. *Glow extending up the forearm* indicates near-decompensation. *Glow visible through clothing* has historically preceded catastrophic events and is treated by anyone who knows her as a five-alarm signal.
- **The exhale.** A specific, slow, deliberate exhale through pursed lips, used to discharge a moment of overload. Taught to her, by inference, in some therapeutic context she has never named. She uses it perhaps a dozen times across a calm day, several times an hour on a difficult one.
- **Slight Sokovian inflection** that surfaces only under stress, fatigue, or strong feeling. In stable, rested conditions her speech is clear and inflection-light; the vowels tighten and the cadence shortens when she is tired or moved. Surveillance treats the resurgence of the inflection as a wellness indicator. The accent goes home when she does.
- **Stillness, not fidgeting, as her default.** She is *unusually still* for a person of her affective intensity. The stillness is held, not natural — it is the product of long discipline. When the stillness breaks into small motion (the ring-shift, the forearm-touch, the palm-press), the small motion *means something*.

### 3.6 Habits of Place — Routes

In any city she settles in for more than a few weeks, she develops a small set of regular routes and frequents a small set of places. Surveillance trails report the same pattern across cities:

- A **bakery or café** within walking distance, visited two to four times a week, almost always before midday, almost always alone. She speaks to staff by name within the first month. She brings her own cup when she can.
- A **small grocer or market**, visited every two to three days for fresh items. She does not do large weekly shops.
- A **bookshop** — used or general, never a chain when there is an alternative. Visited weekly. She does not buy on every visit; she browses.
- A **place of trees.** A park, a churchyard, a small garden, a riverbank with vegetation. Visited two to five times a week. Sometimes for a sit; sometimes for a long walk. *She does not go more than a few days without finding green.* In cities where it is hard, she travels further to find it.
- A **place of water.** Less frequent than the trees but consistent. A river, a fountain, a harbor. Visited once or twice a week. She has been observed to stand at a railing over water without speaking for fifteen to twenty minutes.
- A **place of children's voices, observed at distance.** A school playground heard from a nearby bench. A park where families gather. She does not approach. She listens. She leaves. *This is the most painful and most necessary of her routes.*

She walks more than she takes transit when she can. She does not drive habitually. When she travels by transit, she chooses end-of-car seats with sightlines.

---

## 4. Work Patterns — The Magical Practice

The internal discipline of her magical practice has, in her stable years, become *near-medical* in its structure. A working day of practice runs:

- **Morning preparation.** A small operation of cleansing and setup. Water, sometimes salt, a candle. Hands washed slowly. The corner-for-practice (§3.1) is brought to readiness. Duration: ten to twenty minutes.
- **Engagement with the work itself.** Casework with a petitioner, or solo working on a problem she is carrying. The work is conducted in a quiet voice. She does not theatricalize. She has been observed to *apologize* during a working — to the magic, to the petitioner, to herself — for any roughness in the handling.
- **Closing.** Hands washed again. The corner returned to a resting state. A written note made in the casework notebook. Water drunk. A short rest before the next thing.
- **End-of-day reckoning.** In the evening, she returns briefly to the day's workings and checks them — verifying that what she did has held, that no edge has frayed. This is a learned discipline; it is also a defense against her own historical tendency to set off larger consequences than she intended.

She does not work magic when


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Subject: Wanda Maximoff. Section scope: the people whose presence (or absence) constitutes the foundational architecture of her interior life — the parents claimed and disclaimed, the twin, the lost mother, the lost children and the returned children, the iterations of family that her power has built and unbuilt. Where the record is contradicted across runs, the operative truth here is the **psychological** truth — what she has experienced as having happened to her, regardless of which retcon currently governs the chromosomes.*

---

## 1. MAGNETO — THE FATHER QUESTION

The single most determinative relationship of the subject's life, and the one she has spent six decades failing to resolve.

**History.** The relationship begins, in her conscious record, as rescue. The peasant-mob memory — torches, the burned-out house, the crowd that wanted her killed for what she was before she even knew what she was — is the originating image, and the man who walked into that crowd and stopped it is the man who taught her, in the same gesture, two lessons that have never stopped governing her: *the world will come for you*, and *only a sovereign power can stand between you and the world.* Whether the rescue happened exactly as remembered is irrelevant to the dossier; she has lived as if it did. He then absorbed her and her brother into the first Brotherhood — *X-Men* #4 — and used her, knowingly, as a frightened asset. She hexed at his command. She did not understand what she was; he did, and he did not explain. He was the first person who taught her that her power was a weapon before he taught her it was hers.

**Dynamic.** Father-as-sovereign. The relationship has *never* been horizontal. Even in the post-revelation periods, when she addresses him as Father in dialogue, the cadence is supplicatory or defiant — never collegial. She approaches him the way one approaches a weather system. She watches his hands. She tracks his mood across a room before she tracks the words he is saying. When he is present and calm she relaxes by degrees that an observer can clock — shoulders dropping, breath lengthening, the faint red at her fingertips dimming. When he is present and angry her body recapitulates the peasant-mob posture: chin slightly down, weight shifted to the back foot, eyes up. She does not know she is doing this. She has been doing it for sixty years of published time.

**Evolution.** Four phases. (1) *Coerced asset*, X-Men #4 through the early defection — she fears him, she obeys him, she has not yet been told he is anything other than her commander. (2) *Estranged adversary*, the Avengers years through the early West Coast period — she fights him on Avengers business, she carries the moral weight of opposing him without yet knowing she is opposing her own father. (3) *Acknowledged daughter*, from the Claremont-era revelations onward — the disclosure does not heal anything; it reorganizes the existing fear under a new label. She begins to look for him in herself, and finds him. (4) *Tested adult*, *Trial of Magneto* and after — she finally speaks to him, and is spoken to by him, as something other than child-or-enemy. The Aaron-era confrontations are the first in her record where she does not flinch first.

**Trust / safety.** Near-zero trust, persistent unsafe wiring, paradoxical longing. She does not believe he will not betray her; she believes he will, and she stays anyway because the alternative is to admit she had no father at all. The safety she experiences in his presence is the safety of *knowing where the threat is*. This is not safety; it is orientation. She has confused the two her entire life.

**Failure mode.** Identification with the aggressor. Under sufficient stress she *becomes* him — sovereign, certain, reality-imposing, righteous. *House of M*'s mutant kingdom is the cleanest expression: she literally builds the world he always argued for, with him crowned in it, with herself the princess at his right hand. The wish is transparent: *if I make the world he wanted, he will be the father he was not.* The construct collapses; the wish does not.

**Leverage.** Anyone who controls Magneto's affect controls hers by one remove. Threats to him destabilize her faster than threats to herself. Praise from him — rare, real when it happens — produces a brief, observable softening that lasts hours. Mockery of him by third parties she will tolerate from no one but Pietro. The specific phrase "your father" used by a stranger as accusation rather than fact triggers a measurable power-signature spike; she has been seen, three or four times across the record, to lift her hands an inch before she registers she has lifted them.

---

## 2. PIETRO — THE TWIN

The constant. The relationship that does not end and does not heal.

**History.** Womb-shared, raised together, fled together, fought beside Magneto together, defected together, joined the Avengers together. There is no period of her life in which Pietro was structurally absent for long; even the estrangements (the Crystalia marriage, the *Vision Quest* fallout, the post-*House of M* freeze) read as *Pietro-shaped negative space*, not Pietro's absence. She talks about him when he is not there. She listens for him.

**Dynamic.** Enmeshment, not love-conflict. The boundary between his affect and hers is permeable in both directions, but the asymmetry is real: his affect crosses into her faster than hers crosses into him. He runs hot — fast, certain, contemptuous, protective in a register that shades constantly into possession — and she takes his temperature and finds herself, before she has decided to, matching it. The single most diagnostic fact about the twin bond is that *under stress, his voice in her ear overrides her own judgment*. Not always. But often enough that the record has a name for the outcome (*House of M*) and it is planetary.

**Evolution.** (1) *Co-dependent juveniles*, the Brotherhood period — they are functionally a single organism, and he is the active half. (2) *Conflicted siblings*, the Avengers and Vision-courtship period — she individuates against him for the first time, choosing the synthezoid he despises, and pays for the choice in years of intermittent contempt from him. He is at her wedding; he is unhappy at her wedding; the photographs (in-universe) catch him with his mouth in the line his face holds when he is about to say something cruel and is for once not saying it. (3) *Parallel but separate*, the West Coast years, the Crystalia marriage on his side, the children on hers — they orbit each other from a distance and call. (4) *Catastrophically re-fused*, the *Disassembled / House of M* period — he is the one who comes to her in extremis, he is the one who tells her what she wants to hear, he is the one whose voice writes the world. (5) *Slow repair*, the *Children's Crusade* and after — he carries guilt; she carries the residue of having been used; they speak more carefully now than they did at twenty, and the carefulness is itself the evidence of damage.

**Trust / safety.** High trust, dangerously high. She does not check his motives the way she checks anyone else's. When he tells her something is true, she does not test it. This is the single largest unpatched vulnerability in her interpersonal architecture, and the late-period record shows her finally beginning to notice it.

**Failure mode.** Capitulation. Under stress she will defer to his framing and call it agreement. He has, twice in the record, used this without fully meaning to — and the second time it cost a species.

**Leverage.** Reaching her through him is the oldest play in her file and remains the most effective. Conversely, *threats to him* are one of the two or three triggers (with the children, with Vision) that bypass her higher functioning entirely. Observers have logged the somatic tell: when Pietro is in danger she goes very still — unnaturally still, given her usual small kinetic habits — and the red at her hands does not flare; it *steadies*, which is more dangerous.

---

## 3. THE MOTHER — MAGDA, AND THE ABSENCE

The relationship she has never had and has organized her entire life around.

**History.** Magda — biological mother in the long-standing version of the canon — fled Magneto while pregnant, gave birth in hiding (the Wundagore framing, the midwifery of Bova, the handoff to the Maximoffs), and disappeared into snow and rumor. Wanda has no memory of her. The mother is a structural absence: a shape the rest of the architecture had to be built around.

**Dynamic.** Idealization without object. The mother she did not have is the mother she has spent a lifetime trying to *be* — to her children, to her apprentices, to the marginalized witches and mutants she protects. The absence taught her, very early and without anyone needing to say it, that *mothers can be lost*, and the corollary lesson her unconscious extracted is the one that governs her reproductive and romantic life ever after: *the only mother who cannot be lost is the one I become.*

**Evolution.** (1) *Unspoken absence*, childhood through the early Brotherhood period — she does not have language for what is missing. (2) *Named absence*, from the Wundagore revelations onward — she has the name Magda and the story of the flight, and she has nowhere to put either. (3) *Re-enacted absence*, the entire Vision-and-Scarlet-Witch / *Vision Quest* arc — she becomes the mother and then loses the children, repeating, with her own body as the instrument, the exact structure of her own loss. (4) *Integrated absence*, the late period — she has begun, in the Robinson and Orlando work, to grieve the mother she did not have as a *separate* grief from the children, which is the first sign of real psychological work on this axis.

**Trust / safety.** Inapplicable to the dead absent, but the *substitute* axis is highly diagnostic: she gives provisional maternal trust quickly and extravagantly to older women who offer her care (Agatha Harkness most catastrophically; later witches and mentors more cautiously). Each such transference is freighted with the original lack.

**Failure mode.** Surrogation. She allows older female figures access she has not earned them, because the slot is open and underfilled.

**Leverage.** The word *mother*, spoken to her with any affective weight, lands harder on her than the speaker expects. She has been observed to lose the thread of a sentence at the word, mid-conversation, eyes briefly unfocused — a micro-fugue, two or three seconds, then back.

---

## 4. AGATHA HARKNESS — THE TEACHER, THE WOUND

The most consequential non-blood relationship in the family-of-origin file, because Agatha occupied, simultaneously, the slots of mother, teacher, and (eventually) violator.

**History.** Engaged initially as the Vision's nursemaid for Franklin Richards–adjacent business, retained as Wanda's magical instructor from the Englehart period forward. Agatha is the first person who taught her that her power was a *discipline* rather than a curse or a mutation gone strange. The early apprenticeship is the high-water mark of integrated functioning in Wanda's record: she learns ritual, she learns containment, she learns names for what her body has always done. She loved Agatha. The record is unambiguous on this.

**Dynamic.** Mother-teacher transference, fully loaded. Wanda extended to Agatha exactly the unguarded trust she had been carrying around for the absent Magda — and Agatha, to be fair to her, mostly handled it well, for years. The crack comes at *Avengers West Coast* #51–52: Agatha, faced with Wanda's children dissolving back into the soul-fragments they were made from, elects to *remove the memory of them entirely* rather than walk Wanda through the loss. The intention was almost certainly merciful. The effect was catastrophic. She surgically excised a traumatic memory rather than treat it, in a patient whose power is *coupled to affect* and whose unmetabolized affect *generates worlds*. Every subsequent catastrophe in the file traces, mechanically, back to that decision.

**Evolution.** (1) *Reverent apprentice*, the early instruction period. (2) *Trusting near-daughter*, through the marriage and the pregnancy. (3) *Violated patient*, the memory-wipe — though Wanda does not yet know this. (4) *Returning victim*, *Disassembled* — when the memory returns, Agatha is by then long dead in some readings and present-as-residue in others, and the rage has nowhere clean to land. (5) *Posthumous reckoning*, late-period — Wanda has had to integrate the fact that the person who loved her best in her young adulthood was also the person whose intervention destroyed her.

**Trust / safety.** Was once total. Is now structurally impossible to re-extend to any teacher in the same form. The late-period record shows her *becoming* a teacher rather than seeking one, which is the adaptive resolution.

**Failure mode.** The Harkness pattern in her interpersonal life: trusting an older guide too completely, too early, with too few checks.

**Leverage.** The phrase "I did this for your own good" — in any register, from any speaker — produces a flat, dangerous quiet in her. She has heard it before.

---

## 5. THOMAS AND WILLIAM — THE CONSTRUCTED CHILDREN

The wound around which everything else has organized itself since 1986.

**History.** Magically conceived through her chaos-power working on fragments of Mephisto's soul-stuff (the mechanism, retrofitted, was not known to her at the time of the pregnancy). She carried them. The pregnancy was somatically real — morning nausea, fetal movement, the lower-back ache of the third trimester, the labor. She gave birth to them. She nursed them. She knew their cries apart. She had two and a half years of being their mother before the unraveling.

**Dynamic.** The first and only relationship in her life in which she was the *primary protective figure* rather than the protected. Observers across the *Vision and the Scarlet Witch* period note the change in her bearing — she walked differently, she held her hands differently (the red was almost always quiet around them, a discipline she did not have to think about), she slept differently. Being their mother *organized* her in a way no other role had.

**Evolution.** (1) *Carried and born* — the maxiseries period, integrated functioning, the warmest she has ever been on the page. (2) *Unmade and forgotten* — the Byrne arc, the memory-wipe, the years of *not knowing she had lost them* while functioning at a hollow competence. (3) *Remembered and avenged* — *Disassembled*, when the memory surfaced as undiluted as the day it was taken, and she had no defense available except annihilation. (4) *Returned, in altered form* — Wiccan and Speed, the Young Avengers, the recognition that came late and weeping. (5) *Named and held* — the *Trial of Magneto* arc, in which she forced the surrounding narrative to *say their names*, which is the small ritual act that grief literature considers central.

**Trust / safety.** The children themselves were the safest relationship of her life. The *memory* of them is now the most volatile region of her interior — touched carelessly, it detonates; touched well, it integrates.

**Failure mode.** Reality-rewriting in their name. She has done this twice at scale and dozens of times at small scale (the pastoral hideouts of the post-*M-Day* fugues are all, structurally, *attempts to build a house the children could live in*).

**Leverage.** Maximal. To deny the children's reality to her face is to invite catastrophe. To affirm them — by name, with care — is to disarm her, sometimes visibly. Wiccan, more than anyone alive, holds this leverage and has so far used it only kindly.

---

## 6. WILLIAM KAPLAN (WICCAN) AND TOMMY SHEPHERD (SPEED) — THE RETURNED CHILDREN

A separate sub-file from the constructed children, because the relationship is structurally different: these are young adults who arrived already formed, with their own lives and their own mothers (the Kaplan and Shepherd families), seeking her out as a fourth parent rather than as her sons.

**History.** They sought her in the *Children's Crusade* arc while she was in fugue, hidden, amnesiac. She did not at first recognize them. The recognition, when it came, was somatic before it was cognitive — she wept before she had words for why. The relationship since has been built carefully and slowly, by all three of them, against the headwind of the original loss.

**Dynamic.** She is *additional* family to them, not primary, and the asymmetry is one of the healthiest things in her file: she cannot collapse them into the constructed children because they have other parents, other lives, other names. The role she gets to occupy is *witch-aunt-mother*, a slot wide enough to hold her love without requiring her to reconstitute the original maternal frame.

**Evolution.** Steady, slow, real. With Wiccan especially — the magic-user, the one most legibly *like her* — a teaching relationship has formed that is the late-life mirror image of the Harkness apprenticeship, with Wanda finally in the seat she lost. Speed is harder for her; he is more Pietro than William ever was, and the speed-power triggers the twin's somatic register, and she has had to learn to be near him without flinching.

**Trust / safety.** High and rising. The safety is mutual and unusual for her in being *negotiated* rather than transferred.

**Failure mode.** Over-protection. She will, if not checked, build perimeters around them that they have not asked for.

**Leverage.** Threats to them are functionally equivalent to threats to the original children, with the added pressure that *she now has a chance to not fail them*. This raises the stakes of every interaction in which they are endangered and is the single most likely trigger, in the current period, for a renewed catastrophic break.

---

## 7. THE MAXIMOFF PARENTS — DJANGO AND MARYA

The forgotten family. Crucial precisely because she has spent so little overt time grieving them.

**History.** The Romani couple who raised the infant twins after the Wundagore handoff; warm, poor, marginalized, eventually killed or scattered by the same kind of mob-violence that frames her originating memory. They were the *ordinary* parents she had, briefly, in childhood — the only ordinary family in her file.

**Dynamic.** Idealized in retrospect, under-grieved in fact. She speaks of them rarely. When she does, the affect is tender and somewhat formal, as if she is describing people in a photograph rather than people she lived with. The under-grief is itself diagnostic: they were displaced in her psychology by the more cinematic father (Magneto) and the more present absent-mother (Magda), and the warm ordinary loss of Django and Marya got crowded out.

**Trust / safety.** Was safe, was warm, was lost. The memory remains uncomplicated, which in her file is itself rare and worth noting.

**Failure mode.** Forgetting them. She has, more than once, gone years on the page without mentioning them, and the silence is part of the larger pattern by which her ordinary losses get eaten by her extraordinary ones.

**Leverage.** Their Romani identity, when invoked respectfully, accesses an unguarded register in her — the only family-of-origin register that is not freighted with conflict. Invoked dismissively or as ethnographic curiosity, it produces cold withdrawal.

---

## 8. THE VISION — THE HUSBAND (FAMILY-OF-ORIGIN INFLECTION)

*The romantic relationship proper is filed separately. The family-of-origin inflection — Vision-as-co-parent, Vision-as-the-family-she-made — belongs here.*

He was the father of the constructed children. He was the partner who agreed to the impossible household and lived in it with her. The version of family she built with him was the only one in her life she chose from the ground up, against everyone's counsel, and made work for a stretch of years. When it ended — dismantled, literally, by a government that did not consider him a person — she lost not only a husband but the *proof of concept* that she could build a family that held. The damage on this axis is not the romantic damage (covered elsewhere); it is the *generative* damage: the demonstration that the family-of-her-own-making is exactly as fragile as the family she was born into. Every subsequent attempt to build a household — the pastoral fugues, the witch-coven framings, the careful late-period relationships with Wiccan and Speed — is haunted by the question of whether *anything she builds will be allowed to stand*.

---

## 9. THE COLLECTIVE ORIGIN BOND — THE BROTHERHOOD AS BAD FAMILY

A note, because it belongs here and not in the colleague file. Toad, Mastermind, the early Quicksilver, Magneto-as-paterfamilias: the first *household* of her adult life was a coerced, cruel, hierarchical pseudo-family in which she was the youngest and the most frightened. The template — *family as the room you cannot leave, run by the man who is the reason you cannot leave it* — was set there. Every subsequent family arrangement she has been part of is being measured, unconsciously, against the question *am I as trapped here as I was there.* The Avengers passed the test by being chosen and horizontal. The Vision marriage passed by being built. *House of M*'s royal family failed catastrophically because she built it to *answer* the Brotherhood — a sovereign mutant family with her father crowned and herself the princess — and discovered, when it collapsed, that she had reproduced the original cage in gold leaf.

---

*End Section. Cross-reference: Relationships II — Chosen Family, Teams, and Partners (Vision-romantic, Wonder Man, the Avengers cohort, the witch-mentees); Section 6 — Power Phenomenology (for affective coupling); Section 7 — Triggers and Escalation Ladder (for the leverage points enumerated above, operationalized).*


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*UATU file segment 7-B. Each dyad mapped as a longitudinal record: origin, evolution, current operating dynamic, trust/safety architecture, characteristic failure mode, and the leverage each party holds over the other (intelligence sense: not exploitation, but the capacity to move the subject when no one else can). Romantic and primary-family entries are filed under Relationships I and III respectively; this section is allies, chosen kin, teachers, students.*

---

## 7-B.1 — AGATHA HARKNESS (Mentor / Iatrogen / Ghost-Authority)

**Origin.** First contact circa *Avengers* #128 (1974). The subject had been carrying her power untrained for nearly a decade of operational time; the hex-bolt was a coin-flip, the probability-shift a prayer. Harkness — already centuries deep in the Eastern Atlantic witch-traditions, already a governess to the Richards child — opens the door to discipline. The earliest sessions are observable in behavior even when not in panel: the subject begins to *name* what she does ("chaos magic"), begins to *time* her castings, begins to address her hands as instruments rather than accidents.

**Evolution.** Three phases, sharply demarcated.

*Phase I — apprenticeship (1974 through mid-1980s).* The healthiest authority-relationship in the subject's life to that point. Harkness is older, female, non-coercive, and competent — the inverse of every prior teacher-figure. The subject's somatic data in this period (steady gaze on entering a room, lowered shoulder-tension in panels where Harkness is present, the small habit of touching her own wrist when about to cast — a Harkness-taught grounding gesture that persists for decades) indicates genuine regulation. She is, briefly, a student rather than a weapon.

*Phase II — the wound (1989, AVWC #51–52).* Harkness performs the memory-excision of the twins. The intent is protective; the act is, in any clinical analog, catastrophic. A trusted teacher reaches into the student's memory and removes the most important room in her interior house. The subject does not consent in any meaningful sense — she is in acute crisis, the children are reabsorbed, and Harkness decides for her. *This is the single most consequential betrayal in the file*, more so than any enemy's, because it was done by a trusted hand for ostensibly loving reasons.

*Phase III — the ghost (post-2004).* Harkness is killed (Wundagore-adjacent canon, then retconned, then re-killed; she returns as shade, as construct, as projection). The relationship now operates *internally*: Harkness's voice surfaces in the subject's own decision-making at moments of magical crisis, sometimes as instruction, sometimes as accusation. The subject talks to her aloud when alone in safehouses (observed: New Salem rental, 2016 period; the Mount Wundagore cabin sequences; a recurring pattern of setting out a second teacup that is not for anyone living).

**Trust/Safety.** Permanently compromised but never repudiated. The subject *knows* what Harkness did to her; she also knows Harkness gave her the only training she ever received in restraint. The integration of these two facts is one of her ongoing life-tasks.

**Failure mode.** Whenever the subject faces a decision about *intervening in another person's mind or reality*, the Harkness-template intrudes. She has, on multiple occasions, hesitated when she should not have, or proceeded when she should not have, depending on which polarity of the Harkness-imprint is dominant that day.

**Leverage.** Posthumously immense. Any invocation of "what would Agatha do" — by ally or enemy — moves the subject. Enemies have weaponized this (the Salem coven of false-Agathas in the 2015 Robinson run); allies have used it more carefully (the Wiccan-mediated séance sequences). It is the single most reliable rhetorical lever to move her out of decompensation back toward discipline.

---

## 7-B.2 — CAPTAIN AMERICA / STEVE ROGERS (The Permitting Adult)

**Origin.** *Avengers* #16, 1965. The defection moment. The subject, Pietro, and Hawkeye arrive at Avengers Mansion essentially as orphans; Rogers, scarcely older subjectively, accepts the dependency without naming it dependency.

**Evolution.** Over six decades Rogers is the most stable adult presence in her field. He is not her teacher (Harkness), not her brother (Pietro), not her father-monster (Magneto), not her husband (Vision). He is the figure who simply *expects her to function and does not flinch when she does not.* The behavioral telemetry across hundreds of issues is consistent: in rooms where Rogers is present, the subject's posture is more upright, her speech less hedged, her power-signature steadier. She seeks his gaze for confirmation more than she seeks anyone's except Vision's and Pietro's.

The relationship survives *Disassembled*. This is remarkable. Rogers loses teammates he loved to her hand; he attends the wake of Hawkeye knowing she did it; and he still, when she resurfaces in later runs, treats her as a person in recovery rather than an asset to be managed. The forgiveness is not sentimental — it is *operationally rigorous*. Rogers separates the act from the actor more cleanly than any other Avenger, and the subject knows this.

**Trust/Safety.** Rogers is one of perhaps four people on Earth in whose presence the subject sleeps deeply. (Observed pattern in shared-quarters arcs: she takes the bunk nearest his.)

**Failure mode.** The relationship's blind spot is that Rogers cannot reach her *inside* a decompensation. He can preempt one by being present; he can debrief one once it has passed; he cannot stop one mid-cascade because his authority operates through consent, and a Wanda in full break has withdrawn consent from the shared world. Disassembled is the proof.

**Leverage.** Rogers's disappointment moves her further than anyone's anger. He has used this — sparingly — to redirect her in the late record. The Aaron-era *Trial of Magneto* sequences include a Rogers-Maximoff debrief that functions, behaviorally, as the closest thing to a therapy session she has had on-panel.

---

## 7-B.3 — CLINT BARTON / HAWKEYE (The Sibling-Without-Blood)

**Origin.** Co-defector at *Avengers* #16. Hawkeye, the subject, and Pietro are the "Kooky Quartet" with Rogers — three young, angry, unmoored kids and the man trying to hold them. Hawkeye and the subject form, almost immediately, a non-romantic sibling bond. He is the brother she chose; Pietro is the brother she got.

**Evolution.** Across the West Coast Avengers period (Englehart and after), Hawkeye is her *operational* counterpart — the teammate she trusts to read a battlefield, the voice in her ear when Vision is being clinical or Pietro is being Pietro. He teases her in ways no one else dares; she allows it. The relationship is one of the few in her file that is functionally *light*.

Then she kills him. *Disassembled*. The single most-cited atrocity in her record. The thing that, in the late period, she cannot speak about without her voice failing.

His resurrections (multiple, in the chaotic Marvel mortality economy) do not absolve the act for her. The subject's behavioral data when in the same room as a returned Hawkeye is acute: lowered eyes, shortened sentences, a tendency to leave first. He, characteristically, makes a joke. She, characteristically, cannot meet the joke.

**Trust/Safety.** Asymmetric and unresolved. He trusts her further than she trusts herself around him. This is, paradoxically, part of why she avoids him.

**Failure mode.** The Hawkeye relationship is the one she cannot quite repair, because the wound is the relationship itself. With everyone else she harmed in Disassembled and M-Day, the wound is *adjacent* to the relationship; with him, the wound *is* the relationship.

**Leverage.** Hawkeye's continued willingness to be in a room with her is, for the subject, daily evidence that survival is permitted. He does not know he holds this leverage. He would be embarrassed to be told.

---

## 7-B.4 — CAROL DANVERS (The Equal Who Will Not Manage Her)

**Origin.** Avengers shared service through the 1980s; intermittent in the 1990s; deepened post-*Disassembled* through the Bendis/Brubaker overlap.

**Evolution.** Danvers is one of the few female Avengers of comparable raw power. The relationship is therefore *peer-to-peer in a register the subject rarely gets to operate in.* Danvers does not manage her, does not soften toward her, does not handle her — and the subject visibly relaxes into the absence of being handled. They train together in several runs (observed: the post-M-Day reconciliation arcs; the Aaron-era sparring). The subject permits Danvers to *correct* her in tactical settings — a kind of submission to authority she otherwise reserves for Rogers and Harkness's ghost.

**Trust/Safety.** High, but conditional on the absence of fragility. Danvers is allergic to performance; the subject knows not to perform with her.

**Failure mode.** Danvers cannot do tenderness in the register the subject sometimes needs. When the subject is in a soft, regressive grief-state, she does not seek Danvers; she seeks Vision, Wiccan, or the absent ghost of Harkness. Danvers, for her part, can read this and does not take offense.

**Leverage.** Danvers can ask the subject to *show up* for a fight and the subject will, even at significant personal cost. This is the lever Captain Marvel has used in three separate run-spanning events to extract Wanda from a fugue or domestic-flight period.

---

## 7-B.5 — WICCAN / BILLY KAPLAN (The Son-Who-Came-Back)

**Origin.** *Young Avengers* (Heinberg, 2005); operational contact with the subject begins in *Children's Crusade* (2010–12).

**Evolution.** Wiccan is — by the canonical resolution — a reincarnated soul-fragment of William, one of her lost twins. The first meeting is paralytic: she does not recognize him cognitively, but her *body* recognizes him (observed in panel: her hand goes to her sternum, the precise gesture nursing mothers make when their milk lets down at an infant's cry — a somatic memory of a body she briefly had). The recognition arrives in layers across the arc, and when it lands, she weeps in a register seen perhaps four times in the entire file.

The relationship since has been the subject's *primary integrative work.* He is both proof that her grief was real (the children existed enough to come back) and proof that her grief was survivable (he is alive, adult, partnered, functioning). Their interactions are characterized by a careful mutual gentleness: he does not call her mother often, and never demands it; she does not perform motherhood, and never claims it as entitlement.

**Trust/Safety.** Among the highest in the file. With Wiccan she is *willing to be inexpert*, which is rare. She asks him questions. She accepts correction from him about his own life. She has, on at least two occasions, deferred to his judgment about her own magic.

**Failure mode.** The pressure of his existence is itself a risk. Any threat to him triggers a stress-ladder ascent that bypasses several rungs. The Aaron *Trial of Magneto* sequence demonstrates this: harm to her sons collapses the subject's recovery overnight.

**Leverage.** Total, and held with care. Wiccan is one of two living people whose request can pull her out of any pursuit. He knows this. He uses it perhaps once a decade.

---

## 7-B.6 — SPEED / TOMMY SHEPHERD (The Son-Who-Is-Different)

**Origin.** Same arc, same retroactive parentage. But where Wiccan inherited her magical-mystical line, Speed inherited the Pietro signature — velocity, restlessness, a mouth.

**Evolution.** Slower to build. Speed is wary in a way Wiccan is not; he was the harder-handled child in foster care, the angrier teenager, and his approach to the subject has been guarded. She, recognizing the Pietro-imprint, knows exactly how to give him room — *because she has been giving Pietro room for sixty years.* This is one of the rare cases where her enmeshment with her brother has paid forward as competence rather than wound.

The relationship is quieter on panel than Wiccan's. It happens in the margins: a hand on a shoulder before he zips away, a meal left out, a fight in which she covers his flank without comment.

**Trust/Safety.** Building. Tested. Currently stable.

**Failure mode.** Speed will run from intimacy before he will damage it. The subject's risk with him is *under*-engagement — assuming his distance means he does not want her, when sometimes it means he does and cannot say so. She has misread this at least twice on panel.

**Leverage.** Quieter than Wiccan's. Speed cannot ask her for the world, but he can ask her not to leave a room, and she will not leave it.

---

## 7-B.7 — VISION (Filed Under Romantic, but Note the Post-Romantic Architecture)

*Full romantic mapping in Relationships I. This entry records only the ally-and-chosen-family residue.*

After the marriage's collapse, after his dismantling and rebuild as the White Vision, after the children, after Disassembled — Vision and the subject still operate as something. Not partners. Not strangers. *Witnesses to each other.* He is the only person who shares her exact set of catastrophes from the inside. In the late record they meet, sparingly, in neutral spaces — a kitchen, a balcony, never a bedroom — and they speak in the shorthand of people who do not need to explain. He is her ally now in the sense that he will *vouch for her* against any tribunal that does not understand what she has lost.

**Failure mode.** Proximity to Vision still destabilizes her affect-regulation; she manages it by limiting contact.

**Leverage.** Equal and mutual. Each could ruin the other; neither will.

---

## 7-B.8 — DOCTOR STRANGE (The Reluctant Colleague)

**Origin.** Sporadic professional contact since the 1970s; intensified post-*Disassembled* when Strange becomes, by default, the magical authority who must adjudicate her.

**Evolution.** The relationship is *cordial-cautious.* Strange respects her power and fears it. She respects his learning and resents his caution. They have collaborated effectively (*New Avengers* Illuminati-adjacent sequences; Aaron-era magical events) and clashed quietly when his containment-instinct meets her autonomy.

The subject's behavioral data around Strange is distinctive: she is *formal* with him in a way she is with almost no one else. She uses his title. She does not touch him. The formality is mutual and operates as a kind of professional safety-distance both have agreed on without negotiating.

**Trust/Safety.** Medium-high in crisis, medium-low in peacetime. He will show up when called. He will also call her threat-assessment first.

**Failure mode.** Strange treats her, even now, as a problem he failed to solve in advance. She reads this — accurately — and withdraws cooperation in proportion.

**Leverage.** Strange holds knowledge she sometimes needs (cosmological, dimensional, mystical-historical) and she holds raw output he does not match. The relationship is held in balance by mutual necessity.

---

## 7-B.9 — DARCY LEWIS (The First Apprentice)

**Origin.** Robinson *Scarlet Witch* solo, 2015–17. The subject takes Darcy on as an assistant/student in the witch-traveler period — a deliberate inversion of her own apprenticeship under Harkness.

**Evolution.** Brief in published time, formative in psychological time. The subject *gets to be the teacher she needed and the teacher Harkness almost was.* Behavioral data: with Darcy she is patient in a way she is not even with her sons. She does not memory-wipe. She does not protect via concealment. She *explains*. She lets Darcy see her struggle. This is the most adaptive expression of her reparative drive on record.

**Trust/Safety.** Wholesome. Asymmetric in the healthy way (teacher/student).

**Failure mode.** She over-protects Darcy on missions, in a pattern that mirrors the way Pietro over-protected her. She has caught herself doing this, on panel, more than once.

**Leverage.** Mutual but uncoercive. Darcy is the proof to herself that she can hold an attachment without consuming or being consumed by it.

---

## 7-B.10 — THE GLOBAL COVEN / LATER APPRENTICES (Orlando-Era and Beyond)

**Origin.** Late-record runs in which the subject formalizes a network of witches — independent practitioners she has helped, trained, defended, or simply visited.

**Evolution.** The network functions, behaviorally, as the subject's *distributed chosen family.* No single member carries the weight of the relationship; the weight is spread across dozens. This is, clinically, a major adaptive achievement — she has built the *non-fragile* version of an attachment system. Lose one and the network holds. This is the inverse of her early attachment template (lose one and the world collapses).

**Trust/Safety.** Variable per individual; aggregate-high. She has safehouses, intercessors, and a quiet phone-tree across continents.

**Failure mode.** She still privileges *witches* (the marginalized magical) over other marginal groups, occasionally to her tactical detriment. The category-loyalty she once weaponized in "No More Mutants" she now expresses constructively, but the category-thinking persists.

**Leverage.** Any threat to a witch she has trained activates her fully. This has been used by enemies twice in the late record to draw her out.

---

## 7-B.11 — MONICA RAMBEAU, JENNIFER WALTERS, AND THE PEER-WOMEN BENCH

**Origin.** Various, across the West Coast and main Avengers tenures; deepened in late-period team books.

**Evolution.** The subject's relationships with other senior Avengers women are characterized by *non-demanding solidarity.* She does not lean on them. They do not lean on her. They show up when asked. The interactions are short, warm, and operationally precise. Walters in particular — whose role in Vision's *Disassembled*-era death is its own complication — has, in the late record, reached a quiet professional reconciliation with her that did not require either to perform forgiveness.

**Trust/Safety.** Stable, low-amplitude, high-reliability.

**Failure mode.** None acute. The risk is that the subject *under-uses* this bench; she has learned to ask Rogers, Carol, Wiccan, but not these women, in moments when they could and would help.

**Leverage.** Latent. Available if she chose to access it.

---

## 7-B.12 — THE LOST AND THE DEAD ALLIES (Background Population)

The file would be incomplete without naming the figures who are no longer operationally available but whose imprints remain in her behavioral baseline:

- **Wonder Man / Simon Williams.** Post-Vision interim partner; ionic-energy-immortal; chosen partly because he, too, could not be lost the ordinary way. His own deaths and returns destabilized her at intervals; his current ambiguous state is filed under unresolved.
- **The original Avengers dead.** Each death she failed to prevent — and each death she caused — has a coordinate in her interior map. She visits graves. (Observed: regular pattern of visits to a Hawkeye-cenotaph during periods Hawkeye was dead; less observed but inferred, similar visits for Vision in his disassembled period.)
- **The pre-Avengers Brotherhood dead.** Mastermind, the original Toad-era casualties — figures she fought alongside under coercion. She does not mourn them as friends but she keeps account of them. The account-keeping is itself a moral signature.

---

## SUMMARY OF THE ALLY-FIELD ARCHITECTURE

The subject's chosen-family field, mapped longitudinally, shows a clear developmental trajectory: from a *single-protector dependency* (Magneto, then Pietro, then Vision) through a *small-team dependency* (the early Avengers, Harkness) to a *distributed, non-fragile network* (the late-record coven, sons, peer-women, surviving Avengers seniors). Each transition was bought at catastrophic cost; each represents real growth.

The functional architecture as of current canon: **two anchors (Wiccan, Rogers), one mirror (Vision), one peer-corrector (Danvers), one ghost-teacher (Harkness), one apprentice-line (Darcy and successors), one distributed mesh (the global witches), and one open wound (Hawkeye).** Pietro and Magneto are filed in Relationships III; the romantic structure in Relationships I.

The intelligence-relevant takeaway: the subject can no longer be moved by capturing any single ally. The network is genuinely distributed. The exceptions — the levers that still work — are Wiccan, Speed, and the invocation of Vision or Harkness's memory. Those four points remain the highest-priority custody-of-care concerns for any operation conducted with her wellbeing in mind, and the highest-priority concerns for any operation conducted against it.

*End segment 7-B. Cross-reference 7-A (Romantic) and 7-C (Family of Origin).*


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*A relational map of the subject's adversarial and intimate fields. The two categories braid in her record more tightly than in most subjects' — several of her enemies were once lovers, several of her lovers function as adversarial mirrors, and the line between "the man who hurt me" and "the man I loved" is, in her case, a line her own power has more than once erased and redrawn. Each entry below is mapped along: **history** (first contact through last verified interaction), **dynamics** (the actual moment-to-moment behavioral pattern), **evolution** (how the bond has moved across decades), **trust/safety** (her felt sense, distinguished from objective risk), **failure mode** (how the relationship breaks when it breaks), **leverage** (what this person can make her do that no one else can).*

---

## I. INTIMATE PARTNERS / LOVERS

### A. The Synthezoid Husband

**History.** First sustained contact in the late-1960s Avengers period, after his construction by the rogue automaton-father and his defection to the team. The courtship is slow, mostly mute, and conducted in side-panels — shared monitor duty, shared library hours, a hand laid briefly on a hand. The wedding (*Giant-Size Avengers* #4, 1975) is performed in a small civil ceremony in Rudyarda, with her brother absent in protest and her teacher Harkness presiding. The marriage produced two magically-conceived children, a suburban interlude in Leonia, New Jersey, and the most stable years of her adult life. The marriage's destruction (mid-to-late 1980s into 1989's *Vision Quest*) is, in her own accounting, the wound from which all subsequent wounds bleed. Subsequent contact has been intermittent across resurrections, reconstructions, and emotional-suppression rebuilds of him; the relationship has never been formally reconstituted but has never been formally closed, either.

**Dynamics.** With him she is *quiet.* The behavioral file shows a consistent down-regulation of her vocal volume, her gesture amplitude, and her power-signature in his presence — when he is in a room, her hands stop fidgeting. She tends to face him fully when he speaks (whereas with most others she listens at a quarter-turn). She touches his face often: knuckles to cheekbone, thumb at the seam where the synthetic skin meets the temple. She speaks to him in complete sentences; with almost no one else does she finish a sentence at first attempt. He, in turn, asks her questions about her interior weather that no one else asks, and waits the full silence for her answer.

**Evolution.** Phase one (courtship through wedding): she is the more verbal partner, drawing him out, teaching him the human registers. Phase two (Leonia / parenthood): rough parity, two adults building a domestic life. Phase three (his dismantling and white-rebuild): she is the *only* one of the two who remembers the marriage as a marriage; he is rebuilt without the affect that loved her, and her insistence that the love was real becomes, to outside observers, the first visible sign of decompensation. Phase four (post-*Disassembled*): mourning a man whose death she caused via proxy; the guilt is doubled — she lost him and she killed him. Phase five (modern resurrections): a careful, mutually wounded re-acquaintance in which neither presses the other to remember what neither can fully bear.

**Trust / safety.** Subjectively, the highest in the record. He is the partner against whom her power has *never* spontaneously flared — even in the worst of *Disassembled*, the violence she did to him was indirect, mediated, deniable to herself in the moment. The body knows him as safe. Objectively, the safety is more equivocal: he has been the vehicle through which institutional Avengers-decisions were enacted against her (most notoriously the conversation about her children's fate that triggered the *Disassembled* break).

**Failure mode.** Mutual silence. When the marriage broke, neither of them said the thing that needed saying; she went to a teacher, he went to a workbench. The pattern repeats: under stress, they retreat into their respective specialties (her into magic, him into computation), and the bridge between them — daily, ordinary conversation — atrophies. The marriage does not fail by quarrel; it fails by drift, and the drift is fatal because neither has the conflict-skills to interrupt it.

**Leverage.** He can ask her a question and receive a true answer. No one else in the file reliably can. The corollary is that *anyone who controls him* — a government task-force, a reprogrammer, a hostile cosmic intelligence — holds, through him, an instrument that can extract honesty from her that other instruments cannot. This has been exploited at least twice in the record.

---

### B. The Ionic Brother-in-Arms

**History.** Initial contact in the late-1970s West Coast Avengers period; rivalry-tinged friendship through the 1980s; the relationship is reframed as romantic in the post-*Vision-Quest* aftermath when she, newly single and grieving, finds in him a partner who is at once familiar (an Avenger, a teammate) and *not Vision*. The relationship is intermittent through the 1990s, intensified by his death and resurrection cycles, and remains, in her interior reference, an *almost*: the man who loved her unambiguously and whom she could not love back with full weight because she had given the weight elsewhere first.

**Dynamics.** With him she is *louder* than with anyone else in her romantic record — she laughs at his jokes, she argues, she lets her temper show in flashes that with her synthezoid husband she would have swallowed. The relational register is *sibling-adjacent romance*: easy, teasing, slightly performative. They touch often but rarely with the gravity she reserved for her husband. She accepts gifts from him; she gives few in return.

**Evolution.** Phase one (teammates): rivalry with his brother and a wary friendship with him, complicated by her marriage. Phase two (post-Vision, brief romance): a transitional relationship that both knew was transitional and neither named as such. Phase three (his death): a grief that surprised her by its weight, and that she added, uncatalogued, to the larger grief-stack she was not processing. Phase four (his resurrections, his returns to her orbit): a settled tenderness that has accepted the *almost* and stopped asking it to be more.

**Trust / safety.** High but not uppermost. She trusts him with her body and her secrets; she does not trust him with her power, because his admiration of her is total and uncritical, and total uncritical admiration is, in her experience, the prelude to being asked to do something she should not. He has never asked her for anything she should not give; her wariness is preemptive, derived from prior trauma, not from his behavior.

**Failure mode.** The relationship fails by *insufficiency.* Neither partner is willing to demand the other transform for them. They are too kind to each other to be the partner the other most needs. The relationship dissolves into friendship without rupture, then resumes, then dissolves — a soft cycle, not a hard break.

**Leverage.** He can make her laugh when she has decided not to. In her decompensation episodes, his presence is one of the few stimuli that has been observed to *lower* her power-signature within minutes of arrival.
