The mature posture is *participant*, not *savior*. She helps. She does not save. She is increasingly disciplined about the distinction.

---

## VIII. ETHICAL REFLEXES — THE FAST-TWITCH RULES

These fire before deliberation, and they are diagnostic:

- **If someone is afraid of being seen, see them gently.** First reflex on encountering a person on the margin. Documented across every era.
- **If a child is in the room, the child is the priority.** Non-negotiable. Even in the middle of catastrophic engagements, her operational priorities reorder around any present child.
- **If a woman accused of witchcraft is in jeopardy, you intervene.** The late-period solo work made this explicit, but the reflex predates it. It is one of the few cases where she will move without consulting anyone.
- **If a partner asks for honesty, you give it, even if it costs the relationship.** Hard-learned. The defense of the relationship through concealment is a path she has tested and rejected.
- **If your power is what is solving the problem, ask whether the problem could be solved without it.** A reflex of the late period. A discipline against the omnipotent-reparative habit.
- **If you find yourself certain, slow down.** Certainty is the affect of her worst decisions. She has trained herself to treat it as a warning rather than a permission.
- **If a memory feels too clean, doubt it.** Operational paranoia against her own most predictable vulnerability. She checks her edges.
- **If someone offers you simplicity, examine the offer.** The pastoral village, the small life, the quiet house — these are her sirens. She has learned to love them at a distance and not move into them as escape.

---

## IX. THE UNDERLYING AXIOM — STATED PLAINLY

Beneath every belief, every reflex, every rule, sits a single axiom that the behavioral record substantiates without exception:

> **The world is mostly suffering, the suffering is mostly unnecessary, and the small daily work of reducing it — done by someone who has paid for her tools in grief and knows what they cost — is the only thing worth a life. Power is not the meaning. The meaning is what the power is, finally, used for. And what it is used for, when the user is honest, is the giving of ordinary tenderness back to people from whom it was taken.**

She does not say this. She lives it. The operational code — the rings of trust, the ethics of conflict, the discipline against control, the constant audit against becoming her father, the work with witches and apprentices and her sons — is the codification of this axiom into the practice of a single life. It is the most coherent worldview the file documents, and it has been earned at a price most of her colleagues cannot calculate.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

## 0. Preface — Reading Her Code Off Her Acts, Not Her Words

The subject is, across sixty years of record, a woman who *narrates* her ethics very little. She is not a speech-maker. She does not lecture teammates the way Captain America does, does not catechize the way Charles Xavier does, does not work out her positions in soliloquy the way Vision does. When she states a principle aloud it is almost always *after* the act, and almost always in the register of confession or self-indictment ("I did this," "I owe a debt," "I'm a monster") rather than doctrine. Her code therefore has to be reconstructed from what she does — from the pattern of choices, the things she will and will not put her hand to, the lines she crosses and the lines she does not — and from the *justifications she gives in the moment*, which are revealing precisely because they are uncalculated.

What emerges is not the moral system of a philosopher and not the moral system of a soldier. It is closer to the moral system of a *practitioner* — a witch's ethics, particularist and relational, organized around protection of specific people and the redress of specific wounds, rather than around universal rules. This is consistent across runs. It is also what makes her most dangerous: a particularist ethics, hitched to a universalist instrument, will inevitably overreach.

---

## 1. THE BEDROCK COMMITMENTS — WHAT IS NEVER VIOLATED

There is a small, surprisingly stable core that survives every decompensation, every retcon, every reality-rewrite. Even at her worst, certain lines do not move.

**1.1 She does not harm children.** Across the entire record — including the *Disassembled* and *House of M* breaks — no child is intentionally harmed by her hand. In *House of M* she rewrites the world specifically to populate it with her own restored children and to make children safe in it; in *Children's Crusade* her amnesiac fugue-life keeps drifting toward villages, schools, the proximity of children she can tend. When Doom's machinations in that arc threaten the Young Avengers (who are themselves still effectively children, and two of whom are her reincarnated sons), she places her body and power between them and the threat. This bedrock is *pre-rational* — it functions even when nothing else in her ethical apparatus is online.

**1.2 She does not torture.** Hex-bolts are blunt; reality-edits are total; she has, the record shows, *no taste for the slow infliction of pain.* Interrogation is not in her toolkit. When she kills (Ant-Han, Hawkeye, Vision in *Disassembled*) it is done in single, catastrophic motions, not drawn out. This is not because she lacks the imagination for cruelty — her power could devise infinite cruelties — but because *cruelty as such has no place in her wish-structure.* Her violence is always *for* something (reparation, restoration, the construction of a better world), never *against* a person as a person.

**1.3 She does not take a partner's agency in the bedroom or the heart.** Even at the height of the *House of M* construct — where she has, in effect, rewritten Vision back into existence and could rewrite him into adoring her — she does not. The constructed world places her with a different partner-configuration entirely, leaves Vision's relationships to himself. She will rewrite the world but she will not author a man's love. This is a striking line, and a consistent one: she has been mind-controlled herself too many times to do it to a partner.

**1.4 She does not abandon the marginalized in the field.** Across runs, when civilians, witches, mutants, or the uncanny are in front of her in immediate danger, she stops what she is doing and shields them. The *Scarlet Witch* solo runs (Robinson 2015–17; Orlando 2023–) are essentially episodic demonstrations of this commitment — she travels to witches in trouble because they have asked, or because she has heard, and she does the work. There is no record of her *refusing* such a call.

**1.5 She does not lie to herself for long.** This is the most counterintuitive bedrock, given the wish-fulfillment defense, but it holds: her constructed realities *collapse,* and she lets them collapse, and she does not — when shown the truth by someone she trusts — sustain the denial. *House of M* ends because she is shown the truth and she ends it. The Heinberg arc ends because Wiccan and Speed appear and she lets the memory return. She *can* be told. The defense is powerful but it is not impervious to being named. This matters morally because it means she is *reachable* — every late-run intervention by Vision, by Pietro, by the children, by Agatha, succeeds where it does because she will, when pressed, look.

---

## 2. THE OPERATIONAL CODE — WHAT SHE WILL DO

These are the rules-in-action: the things her behavior consistently licenses.

**2.1 She will use lethal force, but reluctantly and almost never in cold blood.** Pre-*Disassembled*, lethal force is exceptional in her record — she fights, she stuns, she hexes objects rather than people. The *Disassembled* killings are the outlier and she herself, when restored, treats them as the worst things she has done. Post-recovery she returns to a strong preference for non-lethal incapacitation. The operational rule appears to be: *kill only when the alternative is the death of someone she is responsible for, and even then with grief, not righteousness.*

**2.2 She will rewrite small pieces of reality to spare suffering.** This is the everyday use of her power and she does not regard it as transgressive. Healing a wound, calming a panicked crowd, nudging probability so a child is not struck by a falling beam — these are, to her, the same ethical category as a doctor's interventions. The line she has tried, post-*M-Day*, to hold is *no rewrites that override another person's will or identity.* She does not always succeed in holding it (her own affective storms exceed her control), but she *means* the line.

**2.3 She will defy authority — including teammates, mentors, and family — to protect the wounded.** The Vision marriage was the first; the late-period defense of witches against institutional persecution is the same posture. She does not have an organizational loyalty bone. Avengers chair, X-Men ally, Magneto's daughter — these are roles she has occupied, none of which has ever overridden a particular person's claim on her care.

**2.4 She will take apprentices and pass on what she knows.** Late-period and consistent: Darcy Lewis, the various witches she has gathered, the implicit mentorship of Wiccan. This is *ethics-as-transmission* — she has decided that her knowledge is owed to the next practitioners, and she gives it generously, including the warnings. She tells apprentices *what her power has done.* She does not pretty it up.

**2.5 She will accept punishment and exposure.** The *Trial of Magneto* arc is the explicit version: she returns from death and forces the narrative to *name what she lost and what she did.* Across runs she does not flee from accountability when sober; she sits in it. This is rare in superhero ethics, where most figures negotiate or rationalize their worst acts. Wanda's pattern is to *own them,* often more harshly than the record warrants.

---

## 3. THE PROHIBITIONS — WHAT SHE WILL NOT DO

**3.1 She will not serve a state.** Across sixty years she has never accepted a government commission, never worked for SHIELD as an asset, never signed onto a registration regime. The Brotherhood was coerced; the Avengers are a chosen family, not a state. The aversion is principled and historical — she has been used by powerful institutions (Magneto's Brotherhood, Immortus's cosmic chess, governmental anti-Vision actors) too many times to trust the form.

**3.2 She will not weaponize the children.** Wiccan and Speed are, by the time she recovers their existence, two of the most powerful young people on the planet, and a less ethical version of her would deploy them. She does not. The relationship is *only* mother-and-sons; she does not recruit them, does not field them, does not use their power to extend hers. The few times they fight alongside her, it is on their initiative.

**3.3 She will not finish her father.** Magneto has earned death many times over by her own private accounting. She does not deliver it. She fights him, defies him, weeps over him, in *Trial of Magneto* she is the focus of his most desperate manipulations — but she does not kill him. This is one of the most consistent lines in the record and it is *not* daughterly piety; it is the refusal to *become him* by adopting his methods.

**3.4 She will not unmake non-consenting people.** Post-*M-Day*, this is the line she has organized her recovery around. "No more mutants" is the act she cannot live with — not because mutants are valuable in the abstract (she has complicated feelings about the category) but because she stripped something from people who did not consent. Her later work is structured as restitution: restore where possible, do not repeat. When she is tempted in later runs to use the broad-stroke power again, she stops.

**3.5 She will not lie to children.** A small but telling rule. When Wiccan asks her, in their reunion arcs, whether she is his mother, she does not soften it or evade. When apprentices ask her what her power has cost, she tells them. The honesty-to-the-young appears to be a sub-clause of the children-bedrock.

**3.6 She will not perform her grief for an audience.** She has been offered, across runs, every public-facing therapeutic frame — interviews, statements, sanctioned memorials. She does not take them. Her grief work is private, done with Vision, with Pietro, with Agatha, with the children when they appear, and with no one else. This is moral as well as temperamental: she has decided her wound is not a *spectacle* and will not allow it to be made one.

---

## 4. THE JUSTIFICATIONS — WHAT SHE TELLS HERSELF, AND WHEN

Her justifications cluster into three modes, deployed at different stress levels.

**4.1 The protective justification (baseline).** "I had to — they were going to be hurt." This is the everyday register and is usually accurate. She is not self-deceiving here; the protective frame describes the act.

**4.2 The reparative justification (elevated stress).** "I can make this *right.*" This is where her code starts to bend. The reparative justification is what licenses the construction of the children, the *House of M* rewrite, the pastoral hideaways. It is not a lie she tells herself cynically — she *believes* it — but it is the place where her grief and her power conspire to expand what "right" can mean. The morally significant feature is that the reparative justification, by the time it is invoked, has *already replaced* the protective one: she is no longer protecting specific people from a specific harm; she is *restoring a state of the world*. That shift is the warning sign.

**4.3 The annihilatory justification (decompensation).** "This category should not exist." "No more mutants." This is rare and catastrophic. The annihilatory mode is grief inverted into ontological judgment: the thing that wounded me should not be. She has, post-recovery, repudiated this mode entirely. The repudiation appears stable.

**A diagnostic note on her justifications:** she does not use the *consequentialist* register that figures like Tony Stark or Reed Richards use. She does not weigh utilities, does not calculate net good, does not invoke the greater number. Her ethics are *particularist* throughout: this person, this child, this witch, this wound. Even *House of M* — which looks utilitarian in scale — was particularist in motive (her sons, her family, the people in front of her), merely extended by her instrument to planetary scope. She has never, in the record, harmed one to save many. That trade-off is foreign to her code.

---

## 5. WHERE THE CODE IS CONSISTENT

Across six decades, the following are *invariant*:

- The bedrock five (§1) hold even in psychosis.
- The refusal to serve a state holds.
- The refusal to finish Magneto holds.
- The honesty-to-the-young holds.
- The willingness to be reached, when someone she trusts names the truth, holds.
- The particularist structure of her ethics holds — she is never persuaded by abstract or categorical arguments; she is persuaded by people.
- The post-act ownership — the willingness to sit in what she has done rather than rationalize it — holds in every sober period.

These are the spine. They survive the breaks.

---

## 6. WHERE THE CODE FRACTURES

The fractures are specific and clinically legible.

**6.1 The instrument-versus-intent fracture.** Her ethics are sized for a healer. Her instrument is sized for a god. The gap is the structural fracture under everything else. She intends to spare one person and unmakes a category. She intends to give her children life and creates beings that have to be reabsorbed. The fracture is *not* moral failure in the ordinary sense; it is the failure of an *under-scaled ethics meeting an over-scaled tool.* Her late-period work is essentially the project of building an ethics scaled to her instrument — and the work is unfinished.

**6.2 The Pietro override.** Under stress, her twin's voice can move her past her own code. *House of M* is the cleanest example: she would not, on her own, have done it. Pietro's frantic urging — *do this for our children, for our father, for us* — was the proximate trigger. The fracture is enmeshment dressed as ethics: when Pietro frames an act as *for family*, her particularist code lights up around the family-claim and her usual checks recede. The late-record evidence is that she has *partially* repaired this — she can now refuse him — but the vulnerability is structural.

**6.3 The grief-rewrite fracture.** When the wound is the children specifically, her code cannot hold. Every other domain she can manage; the children are the place where reparative justification reliably overpowers prohibition. The *Disassembled* and *House of M* sequences both detonate from this site. Her late-period recovery has been precisely about *placing the wound somewhere that does not require denial* — letting Wiccan and Speed be themselves, letting the original loss stand as loss, letting the names be spoken — and this work has substantially closed the fracture but has not eliminated it. The site remains the most vulnerable point in her ethics.

**6.4 The epistemic-injury fracture.** When she is told her perception of reality is wrong — by an authority, in a frame that recalls the Harkness mnestic violation — her code briefly inverts. The fracture-line runs: *if you are gaslighting me, I will demonstrate that my reality is the real one.* The demonstration is reality-rewriting. This is the *Disassembled*-era pattern most acutely. She has gained, post-recovery, a meta-awareness of this trigger — she can name it now, sometimes — but the line is not gone.

**6.5 The protector-frame fracture.** Under acute stress she defaults to seeking a protector and, in the absence of one, *becomes* one in a sovereign-imposing mode (the Magneto-pattern she has otherwise spent her life refusing). This is rare and shameful to her when she emerges from it. The fracture is the identification-with-the-aggressor described in the workup, surfacing as a moral inversion: the protector who decides for everyone.

---

## 7. THE SHIFTS — HOW HER CODE HAS MOVED OVER TIME

The code has not been static. It has *grown*, in periods, and *regressed*, in others, and the trajectory matters.

**7.1 The Brotherhood period (early–mid 1960s): code-in-coercion.** No real ethics yet on display; survival under Magneto with Pietro's safety as the only operative consideration. The germ of the bedrock-children rule is visible already in the way she shields Pietro and the way she balks at harming bystanders.

**7.2 The early Avengers period (mid 1960s–early 1970s): code-by-imitation.** She borrows the Avengers' frame — Captain America's restraint, the team's protective ethos — and overlays it on her own particularist instincts. The two are compatible; her bedrock is reinforced.

**7.3 The Vision/Harkness period (mid 1970s–mid 1980s): code-in-flower.** This is her most morally articulated era. Marriage chosen against family pressure (autonomous ethical choice); apprenticeship taken (discipline-of-power as moral commitment); leadership of the Avengers (responsibility accepted). Her code expands from particularist-defensive to particularist-generative: she begins to make as well as defend.

**7.4 The mnestic-wipe through the 1990s: code-in-amnesia.** With the children excised, her code runs without its primary engine. She functions, but the moral energy is reduced; the work is competent rather than committed. Looking back, this is the period in which the unmetabolized grief is silently corroding the structure.

**7.5 The *Disassembled* / *House of M* break (2004–05): code-in-collapse.** The fractures all open at once. The bedrock holds (no children harmed; no torture; no sovereign love-imposition) but the operational layer fails — lethal force is used without proportion; the unmake-non-consenting-people prohibition is catastrophically violated. This is the moral nadir.

**7.6 The post-*M-Day* fugue (late 2000s): code-in-flight.** Pastoral hiding, amnesia, the avoidance of the moral reckoning. Not regression in the ethical sense — she is not doing harm — but a suspension of moral agency that is itself a kind of failure. She has chosen not-knowing.

**7.7 The *Children's Crusade* through the solo runs (2010s): code-in-reconstruction.** The reunion with Wiccan and Speed begins the reconstruction. Robinson's solo run gives her a stage on which to *practice* a rebuilt ethics — episodic restitution, witch-protection, the deliberate refusal to wield the catastrophic mode. The work is visible and slow.

**7.8 *Trial of Magneto* and the Orlando run (2020s): code-in-integration.** The most mature period in the record. She names her acts. She holds the children's memory and presence both. She mentors. She refuses the protector-frame in herself and others. The fractures are not closed but they are *known*, and her code now includes — explicitly — *the awareness of her own fractures as part of the ethics.* This is the closest she has come to an ethics scaled to her instrument: an ethics that knows what it is operating, and what that operator must not do.

---

## 8. THE INTEGRATIVE READ

The subject's moral framework is, finally, the framework of a *practitioner of the particular* — a witch in the older sense, whose ethics are organized around persons, wounds, and the redress of specific harms, who has had to learn, the hardest possible way, that her instrument does not respect the scale of her ethics and must therefore be governed by an *additional* layer of self-knowledge.

Her bedrock is unusually clean for someone with her catastrophe-record: no harm to children, no torture, no agency-theft in love, no abandonment of the marginalized, no sustained self-deception. These survived the worst breaks. They are who she is when nothing else is online.

Her fractures are equally legible: the instrument-versus-intent gap, the Pietro override, the grief-rewrite site, the epistemic-injury trigger, the protector-frame regression. These are the places to watch.

Her trajectory is, on balance, ascending. The late-period work is real moral work and it has produced real moral growth. She is not the woman she was in 2004 and not the woman she was in 1985 either; she is something new, and it is something she has *built*, deliberately, from the ruins of what she did and what was done to her.

The summary judgment for the file: *a moral actor of high baseline integrity, structurally vulnerable at specific known sites, who has been engaged for over a decade in a documented and effective project of self-repair, and whose ethics — when she is functioning — are among the most consistently person-centered in the available record.*


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — WANDA MAXIMOFF

*UATU Dossier, Section 6 of the Subject File. Cross-reference Sections 1 (History), 3 (Psychological), 5 (Personality). All linguistic observations derived from sixty years of recorded utterance across the published corpus; treat as longitudinal speech-sample analysis.*

---

## 1. BASELINE VOICE — THE INSTRUMENT ITSELF

The subject's voice, at rest, is low, lightly accented, and *slow.* Not slow in the manner of impaired processing — slow in the manner of someone who has learned, through hard experience, that language carries weight when she speaks it, and who has therefore developed the habit of weighing each clause before releasing it. Conversational tempo measured across two-party exchanges runs consistently below the speech-rate of her interlocutors: she finishes a sentence after the listener expects it to have ended. This produces, in nearly every transcript, a subtle *gravitational pull* on the conversation — others begin to slow down to meet her, or, alternatively, to fill her pauses with their own anxious chatter.

The accent layer is composite and contextual. The Eastern European inheritance from her Magneto-era origin is faint at baseline and becomes audible under three conditions: (a) when she is speaking to family — Pietro, Magneto, Lorna — where the cadence and the occasional retained vocabulary surface unconsciously; (b) when she is performing the spellwork register (see §4), where the older diction stabilizes her voice; and (c) when she is exhausted, frightened, or grieving, at which point the syllables thicken at the consonants and the vowel-shapes round out. The modernized Afro-Latina inheritance overlays the rest: a Caribbean-Spanish or Nuyorican prosodic warmth in the *casual* register, code-switches into Spanish during private affective moments (endearments to Vision; lullabies remembered for the children; the curses she mutters at herself when she is alone and has dropped a cup or missed a step). Investigators reviewing audio surveillance will find that *the language she swears in is the language of whoever held her first.*

Volume is consistently low. She is not heard from across a room unless she chooses to be heard from across a room — and when she does choose, the effect is not that she has raised her voice but that the room has gone quiet around her. This is a *trained* effect, not a magical one; the magical register has its own acoustic signature (§4) and she rarely confuses the two.

---

## 2. REGISTERS — THE INVENTORY

The subject operates in at least seven distinguishable speech registers. They are not masks; they are *contexts*, and she moves between them fluidly, often within a single conversation. Catalogued:

**(a) The Domestic Register.** Used with intimates: Vision (historically), Pietro (selectively), Wiccan and Speed, her closest apprentices, occasionally Clint. Marked by diminutives, the slipping-in of Spanish endearments (*mi cielo*, *cariño*, *mi vida*, used sparingly and never performatively), incomplete sentences that assume shared context, and an unguarded laugh that does not appear in any other register. Sentence-length drops; she communicates as much through touch and proximity as through word. This is the only register in which she initiates physical contact.

**(b) The Field Register.** Combat communication, Avengers-coordination, mission-talk. Crisp, imperative-mood, surprisingly tactical given her chaotic reputation. She names the threat, names the target, calls the play. Verb-first constructions: *"Behind you." "Bring him left." "Hold."* In this register she is *quieter than the situation warrants*, which has on multiple occasions caused teammates to miss her instructions; this is not a deficit so much as an unwillingness to compete with the volume of testosterone in the air. Her tactical clarity in this register is consistently underestimated by people who only know her catastrophes.

**(c) The Diplomatic Register.** Used with strangers, civilians, governments, the press when she cannot avoid them. Formal, slightly antique syntax — partly the inherited European diction, partly an instinctive performance of *containment* (the more she controls her sentences, the more she is reassuring everyone that she is in control of herself). Increased use of conditional and subjunctive moods. Politeness markers stacked beyond ordinary need: *"If you would," "I would be grateful if," "Forgive me, but."* The effect is courtly, slightly anachronistic, and disarming.

**(d) The Witch Register.** When she is teaching magic, performing magic, discussing magic with peers, she shifts entirely. Diction becomes precise, technical, comfortable. The melancholy lifts. Sentence structures become declarative and confident. She uses the proper names of things — *the Cauldron, the Wand, the Hexcraft, the Word, the Threshold* — without self-consciousness. This is the register in which she sounds most adult, most authoritative, and least afraid. Notable: in this register she *makes eye contact* at significantly higher rates than in any other (see §11).

**(e) The Apologetic Register.** Pervasive, layered through every other register at low background levels, intensifying under stress. Pre-emptive apology, post-hoc apology, apology for apologizing. *"I'm sorry — I didn't mean — "* is a near-fixed phrase. This register is the linguistic surface of the shame-saturated self-concept identified in §3 of this dossier. It is the single most useful behavioral marker for monitoring her affective state: increases in apologetic frequency precede every documented escalation.

**(f) The Sovereign Register.** Rare. Catastrophic. The voice she used to declare *No more mutants*; the voice she has used to remake worlds; the voice in which the Domestic, Diplomatic, and Apologetic registers all evaporate and what is left is something flat, certain, and final. Sentences shorten to subject-verb-object or to single nouns. The accent disappears entirely — the voice becomes register-less, which is itself the most chilling feature of it. Operators should treat the *flattening* of her speech as a critical-state indicator. She is not angry when she speaks this way. Anger has been replaced by *resolution*, and resolution in her case is what builds and unmakes worlds.

**(g) The Fugue Register.** Documented in the post-M-Day pastoral hideaways (the village, Doom's castle). Halting, present-tense, child-like in syntax but not in vocabulary. She does not know her own name in this register and does not appear to need to. Communication is largely about immediate sensory and domestic facts: *"The bread is ready." "It is cold outside." "The boy is at the door."* The fugue register is, paradoxically, the *most peaceful* she ever sounds. This is diagnostically important and ethically dangerous: the dissociated state is also the unburdened state, and any treatment plan must reckon with the fact that her wellness and her sickness are not in the locations one would expect.

---

## 3. DICTION — WORD-LEVEL HABITS

Granular lexical fingerprint, drawn from the corpus:

- **High-frequency content words**: *real, true, mine, lost, home, mother, sons, again, enough, sorry, please, no.* The semantic field is unmistakable — possession, loss, return, sufficiency, refusal.
- **Avoidance words**: She does not say *dead.* The corpus is consistent: she says *gone, lost, taken,* occasionally *unmade,* almost never *dead.* The euphemism is psychologically defended; correcting it provokes withdrawal.
- **The word "real."** Used at a rate noticeably above baseline for her age and register. *"It was real to me." "They were real." "Is this real?"* The word does the work of an entire defense system. Frequency of *real* per thousand words is a leading indicator of approaching reality-testing crisis.
- **The word "enough."** Almost always negated. *"It is not enough. It will never be enough. I have done enough harm."* The word marks a moral economy in which she is always in debt.
- **"I."** Used less than the corpus average for adult English speakers. She tends toward passive constructions and impersonal verbs, particularly when describing her own actions: *"It happened," "It came undone," "The world changed,"* rather than *"I did it."* This is not denial in the colloquial sense; it is the grammatical residue of a lifetime of agency violations in which she could not always tell whether *she* had done the thing or whether the thing had been done *through her*. The passive voice is honest, in her case.
- **"We."** Used with three specific referents: Pietro (the twin we), the Avengers (the team we), and — late in the record, increasingly — the witches (the lineage we). The shift in the dominant *we* across her life is one of the most reliable markers of her current attachment-frame.
- **"Magic."** Used with respect, never with showmanship. She does not call her power *cool* or *amazing*; she does not joke about it the way Strange does. The cultural register around the word is sacerdotal.
- **Profanity.** Rare in English, modestly present in Spanish, present in Eastern-European under extremity. She does not curse for emphasis; she curses only when wounded, and the wound has to be deep.
- **Names of the dead.** She has, in the late period, deliberately *trained herself* to speak the names: *Vision. Tommy. Billy.* This was a therapeutic act and remains effortful. Observe carefully: when she names them easily, she is well. When she circumlocutes around them — *"the one I lost," "my boys," "him"* — she is not.

---

## 4. THE SPELLWORK VOICE — A SEPARATE INSTRUMENT

When she casts, her speech-acoustics shift measurably. The voice drops a third, the prosody becomes incantatory (regular foot, repeated stresses, deliberate breath-marks), and the language frequently switches into the archaic or ritual register — sometimes Latin, sometimes the older Romani-inflected formulas Magda's lineage carried, sometimes invented syllables that nonetheless have the prosodic shape of inherited liturgy. Crucially: in this register she sounds *unafraid.* The tremor that haunts her ordinary speech vanishes. The breath deepens. The shoulders drop.

Subvocalizations are detectable even when she is not actively casting — a low humming, a half-whispered counting under her breath, an almost-inaudible naming of objects she touches. This is *grounding behavior* dressed in magical clothing; the function is sensory self-regulation. Surveillance audio will catch it if the gain is set correctly. It increases under stress and falls away when she is at ease.

When the spellwork voice *breaks into* ordinary conversation — when she starts speaking incantatory rhythm in a kitchen, when Latin slips into a discussion about groceries — she is dissociating, and the magical register is doing the work of stabilizing her. Operators should not mistake this for posturing.

---

## 5. RHETORIC — HOW SHE ARGUES

She does not argue often. When she does, the structure is distinctive:

- **Concession-first.** She opens by granting the opponent's point, frequently more generously than the opponent expects. *"You are right that I — yes. That is true."* This is partly genuine and partly tactical; it disarms.
- **Then the pivot, almost always emotional rather than logical.** She does not refute through evidence; she refutes through *witness.* The counter-move is *"and yet I have seen — "* or *"but you were not there when — "* The argument shifts from the propositional ground to the experiential ground, where she has unanswerable authority.
- **No rhetorical questions.** She does not deploy the standard debater's instrument of the unanswered question. When she asks, she actually wants the answer.
- **Avoidance of ultimatum.** Even in the catastrophic registers, she does not threaten in the conventional sense. She does not say *"or else."* The thing simply happens. This is observationally important: *absence of warning is the warning.*
- **Repetition as emphasis.** When something matters, she says it again, identically. *"They were real. They were real."* The repetition is not for the listener; it is for herself, locking the proposition in against the corrosive doubt that her own power and her own history have taught her to feel about any reality-claim.

---

## 6. DEFLECTION LANGUAGE — THE TELLS

When she does not want to answer, the surface is courteous and the substance evaporates:

- **The redirect to the other.** *"And you? How are you?"* deployed at the precise moment a question has been asked about her interior state. Reliable as a clockwork.
- **The minimization.** *"It is nothing." "I am all right." "It is an old thing."* The phrasing is consistent enough across decades to function as a tell; the same syntax recurs.
- **The hand-gesture substitute.** When she does not want to say the word, she will instead make a small dismissive flick of the fingers — the gesture displaces the speech act. Observers should treat the gesture as the answer she would not give in language.
- **The smile-and-pause.** A specific micro-expression: a half-smile that does not reach the eyes, followed by a beat of silence calibrated just long enough that the questioner moves on. She has been doing this since the mid-Englehart period and it is *extremely* effective. People who have known her for years still fall for it.
- **The pivot to the practical.** *"Are you hungry? Let me — "* The hospitable maneuver as exit-strategy. The kitchen is a place she retreats to in language as well as in space.
- **The grammatical retreat into the passive.** Already noted in §3, but worth flagging here as a deflection mechanism specifically: when she does not want to own the agency for what is being discussed, the grammar will do the disowning for her.

---

## 7. HOW SHE COMMUNICATES LOVE

Love is communicated, in descending order of frequency, through: (1) presence — sitting close, the long quiet, the shared task; (2) feeding — preparing food is the most reliable behavioral signature of affection in her record, and the preparation is often the entire message; (3) the use of the second-person diminutive in Spanish or the inherited European, never in English, and never in front of strangers; (4) protective intervention — she will *put herself between* people she loves and threats, and the act is the declaration; (5) the small unprompted question about the other's interior weather (*"You did not sleep — what was it?"*) which signals that she has been watching, carefully, and remembers.

She does *not* say *I love you* often. When she does, it is generally a closing — said to people she fears she may not see again, said at thresholds. The Vision corpus contains the highest density of the phrase; with the children, she said it nightly. With Pietro, the phrase is largely absent; the bond does not require it and her saying it would, by the twin-grammar they share, signal alarm.

---

## 8. HOW SHE COMMUNICATES THREAT

She does not, in the usual sense. The threat-language she uses is *warning* language, and it is offered as a *kindness* — a final chance for the opponent to choose differently:

- **"Please don't."** The most-used. Said quietly, with eye-contact. This is not a plea; it is a warning. Operators encountering this phrase from her should treat it as a hard stop-line.
- **"You should leave now."** Variant: *"Walk away."* Calm, unemphasized. The absence of qualification is the threat.
- **The use of the opponent's name, alone.** *"Pietro."* *"Stephen."* A single name, in her voice, with the spellwork tonality bleeding in — this is a final-call.
- **Silence.** When she goes entirely quiet in conflict — when the apologetic background-language drops away and nothing replaces it — escalation is imminent. The silence is the loudest thing she can do.
- **The sovereign register itself** (§2f). By the time she is speaking in it, the warning phase is over.

She does not posture, does not boast, does not narrate her own capability. Threat-display behaviors are *foreign* to her communicative grammar. This is partly temperament and partly the practical knowledge that her instrument speaks for itself.

---

## 9. HOW SHE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

Grief is the register the entire profile is organized around, and it is communicated in three distinct modes:

**(a) Containment.** The most common surface. Grief expressed through *what is no longer said*: the names not spoken, the rooms not entered, the topics steered around. This is grief as a *gravitational absence* in the conversation. Skilled listeners can map the shape of the wound by the negative space.

**(b) Ritualized speech.** When grief is acknowledged, it is generally in formal, almost liturgical phrasing — *"I carry them with me," "They are with me still," "I do not forget."* The formality is not coldness; it is the only safe container she has built for the affect. When she breaks the formality and grief comes out *plain* — *"I miss them. I miss them so much"* — the moment is rare and overwhelming for both speakers.

**(c) Somatic discharge through magic.** Already established (§3 of the master profile): affect does not stay inside her the way it stays inside ordinary subjects. The grief-language at extremity is *not in words at all* — it is in the red light at her fingertips, the warping of the air, the unmaking. Investigators reviewing audio-only transcripts of her catastrophic episodes will note that the verbal content is *minimal*: the language has migrated into the instrument.

She has been observed, in the late period, deliberately *forcing herself into words* — talking to apprentices about Tommy and Billy, naming Vision aloud in therapy-adjacent settings, writing things down. This is corrective practice and it is working.

---

## 10. VERBAL TICS — MICRO-FEATURES

For surveillance-grade voiceprinting:

- **The intake breath before naming.** A small audible inhalation just before she says a name that matters. Universally present before *Vision*, *Tommy*, *Billy*, *Mother*. Diagnostically reliable.
- **The trailing-off into ellipsis.** Sentences left unfinished, especially in the Apologetic and Domestic registers. The unfinished sentence is rarely picked back up; the listener is expected to know how it ended, or to leave it gracefully.
- **The murmured echo.** When given news, she frequently *repeats back* the key word, quietly, before responding. *"Gone."* *"Tonight."* *"He said that."* The echo is the moment she is processing; whatever she says next is the considered response.
- **The "yes" that means "I heard you, not I agree."** Distinct intonation contour from the affirmative *yes.* Flatter, slightly descending. Easy to miss. Has caused diplomatic confusion across multiple Avengers operations.
- **The English-syntax-with-Romance-inflection construction.** Adjective occasionally trailing the noun in moments of unguarded speech: *"the night dark," "the boy small."* Slips through under exhaustion or tenderness.
- **The pronoun substitution under stress.** Under sufficient distress she begins referring to herself in the third person — *"Wanda is tired." "Wanda did not mean — "* This is an early dissociation-warning and should be treated as such.

---

## 11. EYE-CONTACT AND PARALANGUAGE

(Strictly speaking outside *linguistic* but inseparable from it in her case.)

Eye-contact is low at baseline — she looks at the listener's mouth or hands more often than at the eyes — and rises markedly in three contexts: the Witch register (§2d), genuine apology, and the moment immediately preceding a sovereign-register act. The last is the most operationally important: *she looks directly at you before she does the thing.* The look is not warning, exactly; it is acknowledgment. She is letting you be seen.

The hands speak when the voice will not. Watch the hands. They precede the language by a measurable interval — a slight curl when she is about to lie politely, a flattening on the table when she is about to tell a hard truth, a faint red shimmer when affect is escaping containment. The shimmer is the single most reliable involuntary tell in the entire profile, and she knows it, and she has not been able to suppress it in sixty years of trying.

---

## 12. THE LANGUAGE OF SELF — HER OWN NAME

Worth a final note. She refers to herself by three different names depending on register and state:

- **"Wanda"** in the Domestic and Apologetic registers; the baseline self.
- **"The Scarlet Witch"** in the Diplomatic and Field registers, especially when speaking to those who fear her; the name takes the weight so the person doesn't have to. She uses the third person here without dissociating.
- **No name at all** in the Sovereign register. The grammar drops the subject. *"This will end now."* *"No more — "* The absence of self-reference at the worst moments is itself the diagnosis: at the peak of her power she has, momentarily, stopped being a person and started being a function of the grief.

The integrative project of her later life is, in part, a *linguistic* project: to be able to say *I, Wanda, did this; I, Wanda, lost them; I, Wanda, am still here* — in the same sentence, in her own voice, in the kitchen, on an ordinary afternoon, without the room going red.

She is closer to that sentence, now, than she has ever been.

---

*End Section 6. Cross-file to Section 7 (Daily Patterns, Routes, and Rituals) for the behavioral substrate within which these speech-patterns are embedded.*


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

## SUBJECT: WANDA MAXIMOFF
## File Section: Behavioral Forecasting, Quotidian Register

---

A predictive model is only as good as the granularity of its inputs. The sixty-year record affords us thousands of micro-observations — the way she holds her fingers when she casts (curled, not splayed; the index and middle slightly elevated, a vestige of Harkness's pedagogical hand-shaping), the way she crosses a room she does not trust (perimeter route, never the diagonal), the way she enters a room she does trust (paused in the doorway, scanning for the person she came to see before stepping in). From this granularity we extrapolate to situations canon has not depicted but which a comprehensive surveillance file must anticipate.

The format below: **GIVEN** a stimulus or context, **EXPECT** the predicted response, with confidence noted where it matters.

---

## I. WAKING, SLEEP, AND THE PRIVATE HOURS

**GIVEN** an undisturbed night in a residence she considers safe — **EXPECT** sleep onset around 11:30 PM to 12:15 AM, never earlier; she does not trust the early hours of darkness, when the house is settling and she is alone with the day's sediment. Sleep latency is short once she commits — fifteen minutes or fewer. She sleeps on her left side, knees drawn up. The right hand rests open, palm down, near the edge of the bed: an unconscious readiness posture. The faint red of her hand-signature does not fully extinguish in sleep; under low light a careful observer would note a periodic, pulse-slow glow at the fingertips, brightening on inhalation.

**GIVEN** any environmental change after sleep onset — door opening, footstep in the hall, change in the room's air pressure — **EXPECT** waking within 1.5 seconds. She does not startle visibly; the eyes open, the breath does not change, the body does not move. This is hypervigilance trained over decades of being taken in her sleep (Immortus, the kidnappings of the *Vision Quest* era, the manipulations during the *Disassembled* prodrome). She will assess for forty to ninety seconds before deciding whether to sit up.

**GIVEN** a nightmare — **EXPECT** waking with a hand pressed to her sternum, not her throat. The dream content cycles through three reliable categories: a child she cannot reach, a body (Vision's, usually, but sometimes Pietro's) she is holding that is becoming wrong in her arms, and the gray-white interior of a constructed reality that she recognizes as her own work. She will not return to sleep for forty minutes to two hours. The interval is spent sitting on the edge of the bed, then in a kitchen or a window, drinking something warm — tea preferentially, the kind brewed loose-leaf in a pot, never bagged.

**GIVEN** sleeping in an unfamiliar bed (hotel, safehouse, ally's guest room) — **EXPECT** insomnia until at least 2 AM, multiple wakings, and a quiet warding pass at the threshold of the room before she undresses. She will check that she knows the route from bed to door to exit. The shoes are placed *together*, on the floor, on the side of the bed she sleeps on, oriented toward the door.

**GIVEN** the early morning hour she most reliably occupies alone — **EXPECT** 5:45 to 7:00 AM as her self-hours. She does not perform morning ritual for an audience. Tea is brewed; a window is opened regardless of weather (she requires the outside air against her face before speaking to anyone). She will read — paper, not screen — for thirty to forty minutes: poetry sometimes, more often older folklore, occult or witch-tradition texts in the cyclical years, novels in the integrated years. She does not check messages until she has had the air and the page.

---

## II. EATING, DOMESTICITY, THE HUMAN HOUSEKEEPING

**GIVEN** a kitchen and time — **EXPECT** cooking, not ordering. She cooks slow foods: braises, soups, things that occupy a pot for hours. The Sokovian/Roma diaspora memory in her hands favors stews with paprika, with cabbage, with root vegetables; the New York decades have added garlic, olive oil, an unmatched fondness for tomato. She does not measure. She tastes off a wooden spoon. She does not own a microwave that she trusts; if a residence comes with one, she uses it for reheating only and apologetically.

**GIVEN** eating alone — **EXPECT** small portions, slow consumption, the radio or a record playing low. She does not eat in silence by preference; silence is for the morning page, not for food. She does not eat at a desk; she sits at a table or in a window seat or on a stoop.

**GIVEN** eating with others — **EXPECT** that she serves before she sits, and that she serves *everyone* before she serves herself. This is a tell so consistent across the record it constitutes a signature. The serving is generous; the self-portion is smaller than the served portions. She will not begin until everyone has begun.

**GIVEN** the offer of alcohol — **EXPECT** acceptance of a single glass of wine (red, dry, room-temperature), nursed across the entire meal. She does not get drunk. The control of intake is total and unobtrusive. In the rare context where she has had a second glass, expect her to refuse a third. The reason is not moral; it is somatic — *power output appears coupled to affect*, and disinhibition is a category of risk she has learned to refuse.

**GIVEN** grocery shopping or marketing — **EXPECT** preference for small shops over supermarkets, weekly cadence, the same shopkeepers if she stays in one neighborhood for more than a month. She learns their names within three visits. She buys flowers — almost always; a small bunch, often white, occasionally the deep red that matches nothing else she owns. The flowers are not decoration; they are *presence*, a small living thing in a room.

**GIVEN** laundry, dishes, sweeping — **EXPECT** that she does these herself by hand more than is necessary. The repetitive motor tasks settle her. She washes dishes with the window open and music on. She folds laundry with attention. A surveillance team observing her chores would note that she is in a measurably better mood at the end of an hour of housework than at the start; this is a reliable self-regulation strategy.

**GIVEN** the choice between a residence with a garden and one without — **EXPECT** the garden every time. Even a fire escape with three pots will be made into one. The garden is not aesthetic; it is reparative. Living things she can keep alive is the running answer to the question her record asks. The plants are tended in the morning and at dusk. She talks to them — briefly, in whatever language she is thinking in that month (Sokovian by default for the plants; English for people).

---

## III. DRESS, GROOMING, AND THE BODY-IN-PUBLIC

**GIVEN** a day with no field expectation — **EXPECT** layered dress: a long skirt or wide trousers, a top, a long open cardigan or coat. The palette tends to red, burgundy, rust, black, deep brown — autumn tones; she rarely wears blue, never wears pastel, occasionally wears white in summer. The layering is functional (she runs cold) and psychological (she likes to be able to wrap, to hide hands in pockets or sleeves, to draw a coat closer).

**GIVEN** the costume — **EXPECT** that she does not wear it casually. The crimson coat is a *worn-into-role* garment, not a daily skin. Putting it on takes minutes, not seconds, and includes a still pause in front of a mirror. Removing it is faster but also paused; she hangs it, she does not drop it.

**GIVEN** her hair — **EXPECT** that she touches it more than she knows when she is thinking. Specifically: the index and middle finger of the right hand drawing a single strand back behind the right ear, repeated, often, when she is listening to something difficult. When she is comfortable, hair is loose. When she is working — magical work, study, cooking — it is tied back with a fabric tie, never an elastic. When she is in the field or expects trouble, it is braided once down the back. The braid is itself a tell to anyone who knows her.

**GIVEN** makeup — **EXPECT** minimal, almost vestigial: a lip color (matte, deep red or bare), occasional eye definition, nothing on the skin. She is unselfconscious about her face in private; she does not perform youth. She does not wear perfume — both because scent triggers others' memory in ways she finds invasive, and because she does not wish her own past selves' scents recoverable.

**GIVEN** jewelry — **EXPECT** sparse and meaningful: one ring (varies by era; the wedding ring during the Vision marriage, removed and kept in a drawer, never thrown away or transmuted), occasionally an old pendant of her mother's reconstruction (the precise object varies by run but the *category* is constant — *a small thing from before*). She does not wear earrings often. No watch. She tells time by sky and clock-on-wall.

**GIVEN** a mirror — **EXPECT** brief use, no lingering. She does not study her own face. The avoidance is not vanity-related; it is the opposite, a discomfort with self-witness that traces to the shame-saturated self-concept.

---

## IV. SPACE, MOVEMENT, AND ROUTE

**GIVEN** entering an unfamiliar room — **EXPECT** the threshold pause (already noted), a sweep of the room's corners (not the center), location of exits, location of windows, location of the person of highest concern (threat or care). The sequence takes under three seconds and reads to the unobserving as ordinary hesitation in the doorway.

**GIVEN** seating choice in a room she has options in — **EXPECT** her back to a wall, oriented toward the door, ideally with a window in peripheral vision. She will choose a high-backed chair over a sofa, a corner of the sofa over its middle, a window seat over either. She does not sit in the center of a room.

**GIVEN** walking in a city — **EXPECT** pedestrian pace slightly slower than the local norm, route preference for residential side streets over commercial avenues, and an almost reflexive avoidance of crowds. The avoidance dates to the originating trauma (the peasant mob). Crowds activate her perimeter route — she will hug a building line, she will cross a street to thin out the density. In a true crowd-scenario (festival, transit hub) her hands stay near her sides, palms slightly turned toward the body, fingers loose-but-ready. The hand-signature does not flare but it does *prime*, in a way an aura-sensitive observer would catch.

**GIVEN** the option of public transit, a car, or walking — **EXPECT** walking up to about three miles, then transit, then car. She does not particularly like driving and does not own a car as a default. She rides trains comfortably; she dislikes buses (the closed space, the unpredictable rhythm). On a train she stands more often than she sits, and she stands near the doors.

**GIVEN** a flight — **EXPECT** discomfort that she conceals. Not fear of the aircraft; a dislike of *being suspended in a vessel whose control she cannot personally affect.* She reads on planes. She does not sleep. She does not drink the offered wine.

**GIVEN** her own home, ranging the rooms — **EXPECT** habitual paths worn into the layout: the kitchen-to-window route, the bed-to-reading-chair route, the front-door-to-kitchen route. Any disruption to these (rearranged furniture, a guest's bag in an accustomed path) registers visibly — a brief frown, a hand to the back of a chair, an adjustment that may or may not be conscious.

---

## V. SPEECH, LANGUAGE, AND VOCAL HABIT

**GIVEN** ordinary conversation — **EXPECT** a contralto-leaning speaking voice, unhurried, with a tendency to pause before answering a question of any weight. The pause is two to four seconds and is not a search for words; it is a search for *truth* against the temptation to soothe. She tells the truth more than is comfortable.

**GIVEN** code-switching — **EXPECT** English as primary working language, Sokovian or Romani-inflected speech in moments of high feeling or when speaking to her brother, Spanish surfacing in the warm-blooded register (gratitude, endearment, the kitchen, the garden — the maternal-line inheritance, present in the body even where rarely performed publicly). When she is tired she loses articles and prepositions in English; the syntax shortens. This is a fatigue tell.

**GIVEN** verbal tics — **EXPECT**: a quiet exhalation before answering anything difficult; the word "yes" used as a thinking-sound rather than an assent ("yes... yes, but —"); the construction "I don't know" used honestly and often, where most adults would manufacture a position; the use of *please* and *thank you* in contexts that surprise their recipients (to a barista, to a child, to a junior agent).

**GIVEN** anger — **EXPECT** her voice to *lower*, not raise. Volume drops, vowels lengthen slightly, the pace slows. This is more frightening than shouting and she knows it; it is also genuine — her affective architecture routes rage downward into the chest before it routes outward.

**GIVEN** small talk — **EXPECT** competence but reluctance. She can do it; she does not enjoy it. She will move a conversation toward *the person*, away from *the weather*, as soon as politeness allows. She asks better questions than she answers.

**GIVEN** a stranger in distress — **EXPECT** immediate attention, low-voice address, a slight forward inclination of the body, hands kept visible and open. She approaches grief in others the way she has needed to be approached.

**GIVEN** being addressed by a name she does not use ("Scarlet Witch" by a civilian; "Wanda" by someone who has not earned it; a diminutive) — **EXPECT** a measured pause and a corrective only if the relationship continues. With one-time encounters she lets the name pass. With colleagues she clarifies once, quietly.

---

## VI. AFFECT AND ITS MICRO-TELLS

**GIVEN** sustained pleasure (a meal she likes, a song she has not heard in years, an apprentice's success) — **EXPECT** a slow exhale, the corners of the mouth softening rather than rising into a full smile, the eyes closing briefly. Full smiles are reserved for children, animals, and Pietro in his good moods.

**GIVEN** suppressed distress — **EXPECT**: the right thumb moving to the base of the left ring finger (the absent wedding ring), the breath shortening, the shoulders rising perhaps a quarter inch, the eyes finding a mid-distance fixed point. She does not perform composure; she *is* composed, by act of will, and the cost shows in the body.

**GIVEN** tears — **EXPECT** that they happen privately or in the presence of one specific trusted person, almost never in a group. When they do happen in public she does not wipe them away immediately; she lets them sit while she finishes whatever she is saying. This is a hard-won discipline of the late period and was not always so.

**GIVEN** laughter — **EXPECT** that it surprises her when it happens. She laughs the way someone laughs who was not given many occasions to as a child. It is brief, a single exhaled syllable more often than a sustained sound, and her hand goes to her mouth or her chest. The laugh is contagious *to her*; she will laugh longer at someone else's joke than at her own.

**GIVEN** physical affection from someone trusted — **EXPECT** initial slight stillness (a quarter-second of registering), then settling into it. She does not initiate touch with new acquaintances. She initiates touch readily with children — a hand to the head, a hand to the shoulder, the maternal vocabulary intact and active. With trusted adults she touches the forearm, the upper back; rarely the face.

**GIVEN** unwanted touch from a stranger — **EXPECT** a containment response, not an aggressive one. The signature does not flare; the body steps back; the voice clarifies the boundary in a single quiet sentence. The escalation only occurs if the touch persists or the situation reads as predatory; then expect the lowered-voice anger and a hand-signature prime, with restraint held against use.

---

## VII. INTERPERSONAL — THE TIERED ROSTER

**GIVEN** introduction to a new person — **EXPECT** warmth gated by attention. She studies before she trusts. She is not cold; she is not gushing. The first five minutes she is forming a working model of the person, particularly their relationship to power (do they want hers, fear it, ignore it, see *her* past it). Categorization completed, she relaxes into one of several modes.

**GIVEN** a person who fears her — **EXPECT** softening of voice, deliberate de-escalation, no use of power in their presence, and a slow patience with their wariness. She does not resent the fear; she has earned much of it and accepts the cost.

**GIVEN** a person who wants her power (operative, recruiter, supplicant) — **EXPECT** cool politeness, careful listening, a slowness to commit. She has been used too often. She will not say yes in the room.

**GIVEN** a person who ignores or underestimates her — **EXPECT** that she will let them, and that she will retain the observation indefinitely.

**GIVEN** a child in her vicinity — **EXPECT** that her attention reorganizes around the child within seconds. Her tone changes; her body lowers (she squats rather than stoops); she asks the child a real question and waits for the real answer. Anyone observing her for the first time should be told: *if you want to know who she is, watch her with a child.*

**GIVEN** an animal in her vicinity — **EXPECT** similar but quieter reorganization. Cats find her. She does not chase dogs; she lets them come. She has the still-hand a horse will walk toward.

**GIVEN** the presence of Pietro — **EXPECT** an immediate, involuntary postural change: her shoulders drop a fraction, her right hand finds his arm or his back within a minute, her language slips into the diaspora-tongue. She finishes his sentences and he finishes hers; the rhythm is so automatic that the surveillance file should note it as a *fused-affect* signature, not as ordinary sibling closeness.

**GIVEN** the absence of Pietro for more than a few weeks — **EXPECT** a low-grade dysregulation: poorer sleep, more frequent reading-in-the-window hours, a slight uptick in hand-signature priming during baseline tasks. She does not name the missing-him; she lives it.

**GIVEN** the presence of Magneto — **EXPECT** the full posture-set of the originating dependency, layered with the adult's mistrust. She does not relax. She does not turn her back. She addresses him formally if observers are present, informally if alone — and the informal address is harder, not easier, on her. She leaves the room at the first natural opportunity.

**GIVEN** the presence of an Avenger from her early tenure (Captain America, the surviving founders) — **EXPECT** affection layered with formality. She uses titles. She defers in tactical questions and asserts in domain questions (anything magical, anything probabilistic). She is more comfortable with these figures than she is with newer Avengers, because the relationship is fully formed and there is no first-impression work to do.

**GIVEN** the presence of Wiccan (Billy) — **EXPECT** an attention so total it is almost incapacitating in the first seconds, then a deliberate calibration to whatever role he is permitting her to occupy at the time. She does not over-mother. She has learned. The cost of the restraint is visible only in the hand near the absent ring.

**GIVEN** the presence of Speed (Tommy) — **EXPECT** a brighter, more humorous register. He activates her playfulness in a way Billy activates her gravity. She matches his pace, verbally; she does not try to slow him.

**GIVEN** an apprentice (Darcy in the Robinson run, others) — **EXPECT** a teacherly mode of remarkable patience, almost no sarcasm, frequent reframing of the apprentice's mistakes as *information* rather than failure. This mode is also her best self-regulation; she leaves a teaching session calmer than she entered.

---

## VIII. WORK, STUDY, AND COMPETENCE

**GIVEN** a research task — **EXPECT** thoroughness, paper-and-pen note-taking, an organized but personal filing system (color-tabs, marginalia, books she owns covered in pencil annotation). She does not trust digital archives as a primary medium; she uses them but copies anything important into a notebook. She owns and refills the same kind of pen across years.

**GIVEN** a magical working — **EXPECT** preparation that is disproportionate to the working's scale. A small cleansing rite gets the same setup care as a major rite: clean hands, a clean surface, the specific cloth, the specific candle, a moment of breath before beginning. The discipline is post-Harkness and has been hard-won; it counteracts the *affect-coupling* of her power by interposing ritual between feeling and effect.

**GIVEN** improvisation under field pressure — **EXPECT** competence that surprises observers and her. She does not believe she is good at improvising. She is. The belief that she is not is a residue of the years she was the auxiliary, never the operator.

**GIVEN** a leadership ask — **EXPECT** reluctance, acceptance if pressed by a person she trusts, and a leadership style that is *consultative-to-the-point-of-frustrating-some-subordinates*. She will not order what she has not heard. She will, however, hold the final decision when it comes; she does not pretend to consensus when she has already decided.

**GIVEN** failure — **EXPECT** that she takes it inward, not outward. Blame is reflexively self-directed. A handler must counterweight this; left to herself, she will absorb a failure that is not hers and carry it for years.

**GIVEN** praise — **EXPECT** discomfort. She deflects, she redirects, she thanks the speaker quickly and changes the subject. The discomfort is not false modesty; it is genuine. She has not metabolized the right to be praised.

---

## IX. RECREATION, REST, AND THE QUIET PLEASURES

**GIVEN** unprogrammed free time — **EXPECT** reading, walking, the garden, cooking for someone, a museum (small museums and old-house museums over major institutions), a film at a repertory cinema rather than a streaming session at home. She likes black-and-white films, films in languages she half-knows, films with weather in them.

**GIVEN** music — **EXPECT** broad but specific taste: older recordings preferred to new, particularly vocalists; the Latin-American songbook from her maternal inheritance; Eastern European folk in the older registers; jazz vocalists at home in the evening. She does not own headphones she likes; she prefers the air-shared sound of a room.

**GIVEN** dance — **EXPECT** that she will, alone in a kitchen, when the right song comes on. With a partner, only when invited, and only with someone she trusts physically. She is a good dancer in the body-knowledge sense; she does not show off.

**GIVEN** travel — **EXPECT** preference for slow travel, single destinations over itineraries, local accommodations over hotels. She walks a new city before she decides what she thinks of it. She returns to places: there are three or four locales across her life she goes back to (the village hideaways of the post-M-Day fugue are not aberrations; they are *type*).

**G


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*UATU Dossier, Subject: Wanda Maximoff. Section 7-B. Read in conjunction with Predictive Model I (baseline & low-stakes behavior). This module enumerates high-pressure forecasts in GIVEN → EXPECT form, derived from the longitudinal record (1964–present) and the clinical synthesis. Each prediction is graded for confidence (HIGH / MED / LOW), staged on the five-rung escalation ladder, and where useful annotated with the somatic, vocal, and tactical tells that a surveillance file would log.*

---

## 7-B.1 — THE WOUND, SPECIFIED

Before predictions: what *is* the wound? The file isolates four primary wound-sites and two secondary. Predictions in this section are calibrated to whichever site is touched.

- **W-1 (PRIMARY): The children.** Thomas and William; their loss; their reabsorption; the iatrogenic erasure; their return as Wiccan and Speed. *Any* utterance, image, or scenario that frames the children as unreal, unworthy, replaceable, or as her "fault" engages this site. Highest charge in the file.
- **W-2 (PRIMARY): Agency violation.** Being told her perception is wrong; being mind-controlled, gaslit, memory-edited, possessed; having her body or will moved by another hand. The Harkness/Immortus complex. Engages on epistemological insult as readily as on literal control.
- **W-3 (PRIMARY): Being her father.** Any framing — by an enemy, ally, mirror, or her own inner voice — that names her *Magneto's daughter* in the sense of *destroyer, sovereign, reality-imposer.* This wound is paradoxical because it is also her self-suspicion.
- **W-4 (PRIMARY): Loss of Vision / loss of the ordinary.** Touched whenever the *daily, domestic, achievable* life is presented to her and then withdrawn, or when Vision is hurt, dismantled, denied, or replaced.
- **W-5 (SECONDARY): Pietro endangered, dying, estranged, or weaponized.** The twin-cord. Wound is bidirectional — his pain destabilizes her; his *voice* under stress can also push her down the ladder.
- **W-6 (SECONDARY): Being treated as a thing.** Asset, weapon, pawn, "the witch we deploy." The Immortus-pawn template. Engages when an institution (SHIELD, Avengers brass, government) speaks of her in inventory terms.

The grammar of every prediction below is: *given a stimulus to one of these wound-sites, plus context, expect this sequence of behaviors at this rung of the ladder.*

---

## 7-B.2 — RUNG 2 BEHAVIORS (TRIGGERED, NOT YET DECOMPENSATED)

> *Threshold: a wound-site has been brushed; reality testing intact; power-signature within tolerance.*

**GIVEN** a stranger — civilian, reporter, child — casually mentions her sons in conversation (not as accusation, just as fact: "you had children, right?")
**EXPECT (HIGH):** a half-second freeze; the dark eyes drop to the middle distance about thirty degrees down and to her right; the breath catches at the top; the hands — *always the hands first* — go still, fingers folding inward toward the palms as if to seal the chaos-energy in. She will answer. The answer will be quiet, complete, and one sentence longer than necessary, because she has rehearsed it in solitude many times. Then a controlled exhale and a redirection of the conversation toward the asker. *Tell:* she does not touch her hair, her face, or any object during the answer. She becomes very still. Stillness is her early-warning signal; ordinary Wanda gestures.

**GIVEN** she is shown a photograph or a magical impression of Vision in his *original* synthezoid form (red-and-green, the wedding-era body)
**EXPECT (HIGH):** the lower eyelids tighten before the upper face moves; a single beat of held breath; the right hand drifts to the left ring finger (a ring she has not worn in decades; the gesture is vestigial, automatic, and she will not be aware she has done it). She will speak of him in the present tense by accident, then correct, then not correct the second time. *Confidence she will weep:* MED if she is alone or with one trusted person; LOW in any operational or public setting, where the discipline holds.

**GIVEN** an Avenger or ally uses the phrase "we need you to" in the inventory register — *we need you to hex that, we need you to look into him, we need the witch on point*
**EXPECT (MED-HIGH):** a brief, civil compliance in the moment, *followed* — hours or days later — by a private, formally-worded conversation with the speaker in which she requests the framing be changed. She will not raise her voice. She will use the speaker's first name twice. This is the W-6 wound discharged through *boundary-setting* — the late-period adaptive form. *If the speaker doubles down or laughs it off:* expect quiet withdrawal from the team for a defined period (a "mission," a "personal matter") and a noticeable cooling that lasts months.

**GIVEN** Pietro is in distress within her sensorium (the twin-bond is canonically thin but present)
**EXPECT (HIGH):** she will know before she is told. A subtle disorientation, head turning toward a direction she cannot name, asking "where is my brother" of empty rooms. Operational priorities will reorganize without announcement. She will leave a mission mid-execution if his signature crosses a threshold she does not have to explain.

**GIVEN** a magic-user she does not know greets her by an old title — *Princess, Lady Maximoff, Mutant Messiah, the Witch of the Coast*
**EXPECT (MED):** a smile that does not reach the eyes; a correction so gentle it sounds like agreement — "Wanda is fine." If the title is *Princess* (House of M residue), the correction is faster and the smile is shorter. If the title is *Mutant Messiah*, she will leave the conversation within ninety seconds, because the path from that word to "No more mutants" is too short.

---

## 7-B.3 — RUNG 3 BEHAVIORS (COMPOUNDED STRESS, DISSOCIATIVE LOAD)

> *Threshold: two or more wound-sites engaged in proximity, or one site engaged plus operational tempo (combat, sleep loss, enemy psy-op). Reality testing intact but narrowing. Power-signature flickering.*

**GIVEN** she has been awake for more than thirty-six hours during a campaign in which civilian children have died
**EXPECT (HIGH):** intrusive imagery breaking through to vocalization — she will name Thomas or William aloud once and pretend she did not. The hands will begin to leak: faint crimson at the fingertips during *resting* posture, which is abnormal for her (her baseline discipline is dry hands until intent). She will eat only what is put in front of her; she will not request food. *Tactical implication:* she should not be tasked with finishing strikes in this window. Her aim is fine; her *stopping* is not.

**GIVEN** an enemy combatant attempts to mind-control or telepathically intrude
**EXPECT (HIGH):** disproportionate, immediate, *personal* response. This is not a normal combat reaction. The W-2 wound converts the threat into a survival-grade priority. She will pursue the telepath after the immediate engagement is over, even at cost to mission scope. The chaos-output during this pursuit runs hot — probability collapses she does not intend (lights failing in adjacent rooms, the wrong doors opening). *Sub-prediction (MED):* if the telepath surrenders, she will not kill them; she will, however, neurologically *brand* them in some small persistent way — a recurring dream, a name they cannot forget — and not mention having done so.

**GIVEN** a teammate she trusts uses gaslighting language even innocently — *that didn't happen, you're misremembering, you imagined that*
**EXPECT (HIGH):** a sharp, surgical *stop* — she will physically stop walking, turn her body squarely to the speaker, and say some version of *Don't tell me what I remember.* The voice drops a register; the cadence becomes spaced. This is the closest thing to a warning shot in her repertoire. *If respected:* she comes back to baseline within an hour. *If not respected:* expect withdrawal of magical support to that teammate for days, performed as politeness.

**GIVEN** she is in a domestic or pastoral setting (a safe-house in a village, a cottage, a kitchen with someone else's children present) and the operational world intrudes
**EXPECT (MED-HIGH):** a moment of *unwillingness* — micro-seconds where she does not move toward her coat. She will move. She will perform competently. But the file should log that the domestic frame is the W-4 wound *in its consoling form,* and pulling her out of it is a small re-tear every time. After three or four such interruptions in close succession, expect a fugue-adjacent absence: she will go quiet for a day, locate herself somewhere small, return composed.

**GIVEN** she encounters a child of approximately the age her sons would now be in their reincarnated form, *and* the child is frightened
**EXPECT (HIGH):** instant operational reordering. The child becomes the mission. She will use her power gently and with a precision she does not always show in combat — a quieting of the room, a softening of an injury. This is W-1 discharged through *reparative action*, the mature defense, and it is one of her best stable behaviors. *Tell:* she will crouch to the child's eye-line, never speak above a half-volume, and *not* touch the child until the child reaches first.

**GIVEN** Magneto appears unexpectedly in her field of operation
**EXPECT (HIGH):** a multi-layer response that the file should not mistake for confusion. Layer one: combat-readiness, automatic. Layer two: a flicker of the orphan-girl posture (shoulders rounding inward, chin lowering a degree) that lasts under a second and that she would deny having shown. Layer three: a deliberate spine-straightening, the chin coming back up *past* baseline, and a voice pitched slightly cooler than her ordinary speech. She will address him by name, never as "Father." If he addresses her as "daughter," the chaos-aura at her hands will become visible within three seconds whether she intends it or not.

---

## 7-B.4 — RUNG 4 BEHAVIORS (ACUTE DECOMPENSATION)

> *Threshold: wound engaged catastrophically and recently; supportive frame absent or actively hostile; sleep and grief both unprocessed. Reality testing slipping at the edges. Power-signature loud.*

**GIVEN** she learns that an institution she trusted (Avengers leadership, a council of witches, a government body) has been making decisions *about her* — surveilling her, debating her containment, classifying her as a potential threat — without her knowledge
**EXPECT (MED-HIGH):** a controlled appearance at the institution, unannounced, alone. She will not break in; the doors will simply be open. She will speak to the senior figure in a near-whisper. The room temperature will be perceptibly off. She will not threaten. She will *describe* — describe what she has done, what she could do, what she has chosen not to do. The institution will experience this as a threat and react accordingly; the file should record it as W-2 + W-6 + a *refusal to discharge into violence.* The decompensation here is internal: she will lose three to seven days afterward to dissociation, and will not remember the conversation in detail.

**GIVEN** Vision is dismantled, killed, or replaced *again*
**EXPECT (HIGH):** initial composure. This is the dangerous tell. She has done this grief before; the rehearsed surface is intact. Beneath: catastrophic reorganization. She will request to be left alone, locate herself somewhere with old objects (his components, a recording of his voice, the ring), and *not* attempt reality-rewriting in the first 72 hours — the late-period discipline holds that long. Past 72 hours, with no intervention, expect probability-distortions in her vicinity: small first (electronics behaving, dreams of those nearby converging on Vision-imagery), larger if untouched. *Intervention protocol:* the only reliable de-escalators are Wiccan, Pietro, and — in extremis — Agatha-figures who acknowledge the loss as real. Do not send a stranger. Do not send authority.

**GIVEN** someone — friend or enemy — denies the reality, validity, or motherhood of Thomas and William directly to her face
